Wu Tiecheng Passes Through Shenyang to Harbin

Will Go to Beidaihe for Summer Vacation

Talks Regarding Guangdong Affairs

Shenyang Correspondence: Member of the Central Executive Committee Wu Tiecheng, because the Administrative Director of the Harbin Special District, Zhang Jinghui, will celebrate his sixtieth birthday on the 19th of this month, departed from Beijing on the 15th to congratulate him on behalf of General Chiang. When he passed through Tianjin on the 17th, he visited the Chairman of Hebei Province, Wang Shuchang, for a meeting. He then took the third train of the Beining Railway to Liaoning, arriving at the Shenyang South Manchuria Railway Station at 8:00 AM on the 18th, and disembarked. Few people knew about Wu's arrival in advance, so only the Deputy Director of the Beining Railway, Lao Mian, and the Assistant Manager of the Liaoning Traffic Bank, Li, greeted him. After getting off the train, he went to the Kaining Hotel to rest and have breakfast. Wu's secretaries, Xiao Tongzi and Zhang Zhenxi, also came with him. Wu's wife also accompanied him. Lao Mian invited him to a banquet at the Lumingchun Restaurant, and then they went to visit various dignitaries. In the afternoon at 3:30 PM, he took the South Manchuria Railway train to Changchun, transferring to Harbin. After Wu arrived in Shenyang, the reporter immediately visited him. Wu said that this trip was for no important business, but to congratulate Chief Zhang Xuwu on his birthday. He will return to Shenyang the next day to participate in the third anniversary of Zhang Zuolin's death. After that, he will go to Ping to see Vice Commander Zhang's illness. He himself has been suffering from a cough recently and will not stay in Ping for long, but will go to Beidaihe for summer vacation to rest. The reporter asked whether Hu Hanmin and Li Jishen would soon take up the positions of National Committee members. He replied that the Central Government earnestly hoped that Mr. Hu would soon share the important task of the Party and the country. Hu had already agreed to take up the position of National Committee member, but because his health had not fully recovered, he would first go to the United States for recuperation, which had been approved by the Central Government, and hoped that he would return soon to assist in national affairs. He did not clearly know whether Li Jishen would take up the position of National Committee member. Since Zhang Puquan went to Guangdong to convey the intentions of the Central Government, the hope for peace has increased. The Central Government is determined to pursue peace to the end and concentrate all its efforts on suppressing the Communists. General Chiang will go to Jiangxi soon, and the comrades in Guangdong are also very eager for peace and recognize that the Central Government's all-out effort to suppress the Communists is the most urgent task. As for the peaceful solution, it is currently under discussion. (June 18)

Three Major Specialties of the Anfeng Railway Line

Tussah Silk, Yellow Tobacco, and Paddy Fields

Andong Correspondence: Although the Anfeng Railway line and the Yalu River coast are deep in the mountains and forests, with barren soil, and cannot be compared to the fertile fields of the interior, the eastern section of the Anfeng Railway has a suitable climate. Moreover, because the railway runs through it, directly connecting Manchuria and Korea, transportation is convenient. Therefore, the three major specialties of the eastern border, such as tussah silk, yellow tobacco, and paddy fields, have developed year by year, surpassing the interior and becoming a major source of income in the newly developed eastern border. The situation in the Fengcheng area in the eastern section of the Anfeng Railway is investigated as follows: (1) Tussah Silk: The southern part of Fengcheng County has rivers running crisscross, suitable for planting rice. The northern part has overlapping mountains and ridges, suitable for raising tussah silkworms. The central part has fertile soil, most suitable for planting yellow tobacco. Therefore, the three major specialties have developed very rapidly. In the eleventh year of the Republic of China, the Fengtian Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau established a water conservancy sub-bureau in Fengcheng County and sent personnel to the countryside to encourage farmers to plant rice. At that time, most farmers did not know about water conservancy and were quite hesitant. Disputes often arose over ditching and water diversion. Later, the low-lying land that was unsuitable for cultivating other crops was converted to rice cultivation, gradually gaining substantial profits, and farmers began to imitate planting, so the paddy fields developed from this. As of the end of the nineteenth year, the paddy fields in the entire territory of Fengcheng had reached 34,700 mu. On average, each mu yields five dou of rice, with a total annual harvest of more than 520,500 shi. If officials and the people can work together to promote it, the development of paddy fields will be unlimited. (3) Tussah Silk: The entire territory of Fengcheng has 15,572 silkworm shears (each silkworm shear can raise 5,000 cocoon seeds, which is called a "shear," which is a common name among farmers. Farmers in the eastern province who raise silkworms all use this term). Silkworms are raised twice a year, in spring and autumn. Spring silkworms go up the mountain during Grain Rain and the cocoons are harvested in early summer. Autumn silkworms go up the mountain during midsummer and the cocoons are harvested during Cold Dew. Last year, in the spring and autumn seasons, a total of 500,000 "qian" were harvested. (Tussah silkworm transactions are based on 1,000 pieces as a unit. For example, 10,000 pieces are called "ten qian," not "ten thousand.") Because Fengcheng has no silk factory, the cocoons produced must be transported to Andong for sale, or silk merchants go to the area to buy them. (3) Yellow Tobacco: In the ninth year of the Republic of China, the Dalian South Manchuria Railway Company promoted the yellow tobacco industry and sent specialists to establish a yellow tobacco experimental farm at Fengcheng Station, purchasing American yellow tobacco seeds for trial planting. Because the soil and climate are suitable, the first year's trial planting was very successful. In the second year, the scope was expanded, and the South Manchuria Railway Company directly invested 500,000 yuan to create a yellow tobacco cooperative, recruiting people from China, Japan, and Korea who had experience in growing tobacco as cooperative members. At the beginning, Chinese people hesitated to join. The cooperative used profits to attract them, giving generous rents to landlords and lending money to Chinese people to encourage them to try growing yellow tobacco. Chinese people then joined in large numbers. After the autumn settlement, the profits were very high. In addition to repaying principal and interest, there were still some remaining profits. By the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, the cooperative had a total of 115 Chinese, Japanese, and Korean cooperative members, growing a total of 600 "tian" of yellow tobacco (every six mu is one "tian"). Each mu yields about 50 catties. After the autumn harvest, all were handed over to the cooperative and resold to British, American, East Asian, and other tobacco companies. (The British American Tobacco Company, which produces Hardman cigarettes, has a factory in the capital of Liaoning Province, and its raw materials are supplied by the yellow tobacco of Fengcheng.) In the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, the Fengcheng County Government, recognizing that the Japanese yellow tobacco cooperative had achieved effective results, also convened a meeting of gentry and merchants to create a tobacco industry association, which was unanimously supported and established immediately, promoting self-cultivation of yellow tobacco. Officials and people invested and joined in large numbers, with unusual enthusiasm. As of the autumn of the nineteenth year, the association had reached more than 100 members, growing a total of 500 "tian" of yellow tobacco. The yellow tobacco produced was sold to the British American Tobacco Company. The funds used by the tobacco industry association were advanced by the British American Tobacco Company. Only five years have passed since the establishment of the association, and it has already achieved such profits. The future development prospects are truly unlimited. (June 16)

Anhui Provincial Government Orders Counties to Eradicate Opium Seedlings

But Local Officials Still Levy Opium Tax

Bengbu Correspondence: The opium scourge in northern Anhui has been widespread for a long time. The opium prohibition has been lax for years and has not been cleared up. Unexpectedly, this year, the opium seedlings in Su, Si, Meng, Wo, Hao, Tai, Ying, Fu, and other counties are especially numerous, and the reason is that the officials levy opium tax, which is all the rage. The district party headquarters here has reported to the provincial party headquarters and asked the provincial government to order the counties in northern Anhui to effectively clear up opium. Those who violate the order will be punished. After the provincial government approved the letter, it recently issued instructions to the county magistrates of the aforementioned counties, stating: "The letter No. 3626 from the Anhui Provincial Party Affairs Reorganization Committee has been approved. The Bengbu District Party Affairs Reorganization Committee reported that it requested the provincial government to order the counties in northern Anhui to effectively clear up opium and punish those who violate the order. Opium is an extremely harmful substance, and the counties in Anhui have suffered from it for more than a year. Since the National Government issued a general ban on opium, we expected to clear up the poisonous plants and eliminate the source of the scourge forever. However, according to reports, the counties in northern Anhui are still levying opium tax from the people and privately collecting seedling tax. We are heartbroken and shocked to hear this. The county magistrates are officials under the rule of the Party, and should be honest and self-disciplined, and serve as the protector of the people. Unexpectedly, they dare to engage in corruption and oppress our people, violating the Premier's instructions to reject opium, which is truly unforgivable. In addition to sending letters to the party headquarters of the counties in northern Anhui, urging them to investigate and ban opium within a specified period, and expanding publicity so that the public is deeply aware of the harm of opium and is not deceived by corruption, we report the situation and request that the Council examine and approve it, and order strict prohibition by the provincial government to comply with the Party's teachings and benefit the people." Therefore, in addition to instructions and distribution, the county magistrates are immediately ordered to comply, conduct a thorough investigation, and strictly eradicate opium, without any slackness, lest they incur serious guilt. The investigation and eradication situation must be reported at any time. Sincerely ordered." (19th)

Finance in Shandong After Abolishing Likin

Jinan Correspondence: Since the abolition of likin in Shandong Province, the financial situation has been quite optimistic after active reorganization by the Department of Finance. According to what Weng Zhiquan, the chief secretary of the Department of Finance, said recently, it is quite detailed. After the Central Army recovered Jinan last year, Wang Xiangrong, the head of the Department of Finance, took office on September 9. At that time, the cash in the treasury was only three or four thousand yuan, while the accumulated debt for education and justice expenses amounted to one million six hundred thousand yuan. After investigation, it was found that the counties owed more than two million yuan in miscellaneous taxes during the tenure of the former head of the department, Yuan Jiapu. After repeated rectification, the financial revenue gradually improved. Now, the monthly revenue is two million yuan, and the expenditure is about one million five hundred and sixty thousand yuan. The revenue of last month is enough to cover the expenses of the next month plus ten days. As of the end of May, the surplus was seven or eight hundred thousand yuan. Because the education expenses are mostly relied on by poor scholars for living, and the justice expenses are related to the food supply of prisoners, the one million six hundred thousand yuan owed by the former head of the department, Yuan, for education and justice expenses last year has been repaid by eight hundred thousand yuan, and the remaining amount will be repaid as soon as possible to clear the debt. After the abolition of likin, the Central Government has provided funds of 1.234 million in total for four months, 200,000 each month, plus 200,000 at the end of the year, totaling one million yuan, which have already been remitted. The business tax is about to be implemented, and the financial future is very promising. At present, a universal collection and expenditure method is implemented. The funds within the budget must be paid in full, and no one is allowed to have the previous habit of deducting and using them separately. Fortunately, all the measures have been implemented as desired. All the preparations for the business tax have been completed, and the director's candidate will be announced soon.

Qingdao

Disputes Between Chinese and Japanese Merchants in the Exchange

Qingdao Correspondence: The Qingdao Exchange is nominally jointly operated by Chinese and Japanese merchants, but all the major powers are controlled by the Japanese, which is nothing less than the only monopoly institution for Japanese merchants in Qingdao. Recently, Chinese and Japanese merchants in the Exchange suddenly had a dispute over trading issues, and then even resorted to violence, which is almost unprecedented in international trade. The incident originated from the Japanese firm Zhengsheng, which sold 1,100 tons of July-term rice on the Exchange in mid-May to a Chinese merchant at a price of nine yuan per hundred catties. The current price has risen to ten yuan and three jiao. The Japanese merchant was afraid that the price would continue to rise and inevitably suffer losses, so he deliberately made trouble and shouted in the market to sell July-term rice at nine yuan and three jiao. Many Chinese merchants then traded with him, and when they asked him to issue an order, he deliberately shirked responsibility. The Chinese merchants, seeing that he was deliberately disrupting the market price and repeatedly breaking his promise, immediately argued with him. He was stubborn and unreasonable, starting with verbal abuse and then resorting to violence. Later, with the efforts of the police and the Exchange staff, the situation was not expanded. However, all the native Chinese merchants, provoked by public outrage, withdrew from the Exchange from the next day and traded at the Qiyan Assembly Hall, specializing in spot goods and not ordering futures. The Exchange, because of the withdrawal of Chinese merchants and trading outside, was concerned about its reputation, so on the 18th of this month, at 4:00 PM, Chinese and Japanese members held a meeting to mediate. The Chinese members present were Liang Hepu, Zhang Litang, Qi Dechen, Shang Shuguan, Shou Huatang, and Zhang Junqing, while the Japanese members present were Mitsui, Donghe, Tailai, Mitsubishi, and Yoshizawa. The meeting discussed the mediation method. It was agreed that the Japanese firm Zhengsheng's two transactions of 1,100 tons of rice each were in violation of the Exchange's rules and should be fined 3% according to the regulations. The Japanese, knowing that they were wrong, were willing to admit the penalty for the first transaction of 1,100 tons, but for the second transaction of 1,100 tons, they argued that they had not paid the deposit or issued an order, hoping to evade responsibility. The Japanese members also defended them. However, because the Chinese side had sufficient reasons, the Japanese had no way out and finally requested that the second transaction be punished lightly. It is said that the Chinese merchants were also willing to agree. The dispute can now be expected to be resolved. (June 18)

Hunan Province

Reason for Stoppage of Immigration to Jilin

The Jilin Provincial Government Claims Inability to Provide Accommodation

The Ministry Orders the Railway Bureau Not to Transport

A Changsha dispatch states that the Hunan Provincial Relief Committee established a reclamation office in Yilan County, Jilin Province, and appointed Cao Ji as its director. It planned to transfer 1,000 disaster victims from Hunan for reclamation. The first batch of 500 disaster victims was scheduled to begin transportation on the 20th of this month. A grand immigration ceremony was planned for that day at the Provincial Relief Committee, inviting leaders from the party, government, and military to participate. Meanwhile, Yang Jichang was sent to Hankou, and Zhou Fengzao to Peiping and Harbin, to negotiate for free transportation by railcars and to take care of everything. Yang and Zhou departed several days ago. The luggage of all disaster victims has now been prepared for departure. At the same time, many small business owners have organized a "Northeast Immigration and Reclamation Hunan Small Business Investigation Group" intending to go along to operate industrial and commercial businesses. All sectors of Hunan society have expressed great sympathy for this and are preparing to see them off at the time of departure. Unexpectedly, the Jilin Provincial Government suddenly prevented the Hunan disaster victims from going, and the Xiang-E (Hunan-Hubei) Railway Bureau also received an order from the Ministry not to transport them. The telegram from the Ministry of Railways to the Hunan Provincial Government is recorded as follows: "Previously, your government's document No. 5626 regarding the transportation of 1,000 disaster victims from the Hunan Provincial Relief Committee to Yilan County, Jilin, for reclamation and requesting free transportation has been replied to by this Ministry in document No. 2777. Now, according to a telegram from the Northeast Transportation Committee, it has been found that regarding the Hunan Provincial Relief Committee's transfer of 1,000 disaster victims to Yilan County, Jilin, for reclamation, this committee, having no record to verify, telegraphed the Northeast Political Affairs Committee for instructions. The Northeast Political Affairs Committee replied that the Hunan immigration matter had been ordered to the Jilin Provincial Government for a quick investigation and response. The reply stated that because disaster victims from Henan Province had previously been ordered to be accommodated, Yilan County was instructed to investigate and respond, and it was reported that there was no land available for allocation and no way to accommodate them. The current situation with Hunan is the same, and it is difficult to immediately permit the transfer. Moreover, the number of refugees is large, their quality is uneven, and the people and land may not be suitable, which could lead to abuses. We should request a telegram to prevent them from going to avoid displacement. The various points mentioned by the provincial government are consistent with the actual situation. In addition to issuing instructions to approve them, this order instructs the association to investigate and handle accordingly, and to send a telegram to prevent them from proceeding, to avoid displacement. It has been found that since Yilan County, Jilin, has no way to accommodate the Hunan disaster victims, we should ask the Ministry of Transportation to quickly send a telegram to prevent them from coming north to avoid displacement. A corresponding telegram is sent in reply, requesting investigation and handling." Since the above situation has been reported, in addition to sending telegrams to the relevant county bureaus to investigate and handle accordingly, a corresponding telegram is sent to request your government to find a way to prevent them from going north, to avoid displacement. He Jian received the telegram and believed that the transfer of Hunan disaster victims to Yilan for reclamation had been preceded by the selection of reclaimed land there. Zhang Zuce from Hunan had also been operating industrial and commercial businesses there for a long time, and Hunan could accommodate more than 10,000 disaster victims. Zhang Zuce had personally come to Hunan and signed a reclamation contract with the Hunan Provincial Government. The Jilin Provincial Government's statement that there was no wasteland available for accommodation was a misunderstanding. He decided to reply to the Ministry of Railways with an explanation, requesting that the transfer still be permitted to provide relief to the disaster victims. (June 18)

Wuhu Express News

Today (15th) at 2:00 PM, various sectors held a meeting at the County Party Headquarters to discuss and decide to establish the Wuhu All Sectors Committee for Recovering Church Properties. The Wuhu County Government has received this order and today sent a special letter to the British and American Consulates General in Beijing and the Japanese Consulate in Wuhu, informing foreign nationals in Wuhu to comply. The Wuhu Catholic Church has now realized the situation and has sent teacher Kang to the government to declare that they are willing to comply with the registration form and submit to the handling of all church properties.

Regarding the previous robbery of the Beijing-Wuhu small steamboat in Wujiang, the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs has ordered the county governments of Wuhu and Dangtu to protect the operation of the Beijing-Wuhu small steamboats and to conduct strict inspections of passengers at various ports to prevent bandits from hiding and endangering travelers.

The Jiang family, residents near the HSBC Rice Mill on the south bank, was robbed by bandits this morning and suffered significant losses.

Local News

Songjiang

Bandits Kidnap and Extort Ransom. The family of Gu Genbo, a villager in Caobang Township, Xiaokunshan Township, more than ten li from the city, was suddenly attacked by more than ten kidnappers speaking a mixed dialect of local and Hakka voices the night before last. They broke into the house, rummaged through boxes and cabinets, and finding no valuable clothing, they did not get what they wanted. They tied up Gu's four sons and claimed they needed a ransom of 2,300 yuan. Gu's father, deeply loving his sons, pleaded in every possible way and finally collected 500 yuan to hand over before the four sons were released. The remaining 1,800 yuan was scheduled to be paid later. The kidnappers then left triumphantly. The victim, fearing the power of the bandits, dared not report to the authorities and it is also heard that the remaining money has been collected and delivered. It is rumored that the bandits are currently gathering in Liuta and other places, specializing in kidnapping.

Wuxi

Police School Students Commit Violence. Yu Tongjiang (also known as Yu San), a resident of Jiancheng, lives under the Bianmin Bridge in the southern part of the city. He previously sublet vehicles on behalf of Xu Yaoqing, the owner of the Defeng Rickshaw Company next door. Last winter, he left Defeng and sublet rickshaws with Shuntai. The day before yesterday morning, Yu Zhongjiang had a quarrel with Xu Bixian, a vehicle releaser from Defeng. They wrestled each other to the派出所(branch police station) of the First Public Security Bureau. Because their words differed,巡長(patrol leader) Xu Yunsheng went to the scene to investigate and mediate. Unexpectedly, Dai Shunzhi (a native of the county who lives in front of the new temple in the city), Xu Huang (from Xuzhou), and another man, graduates of the Zhenjiang Police Officer School, wearing military uniforms, beat Yu San severely in the 派出所 because of a disagreement, causing him serious injuries. He immediately fell to the ground and could not speak. Patrol Leader Xu returned and saw the situation and took the three men, Dai Shunzhi, into custody. He immediately reported to the First Public Security Bureau and summoned a Western doctor for treatment, but he still could not speak. The branch bureau transferred them to the County Public Security Bureau and then to the County Court, where Prosecutor Du opened a court session. At that time, Yu San was able to speak slightly and voluntarily requested to delay medical treatment to see how the injury developed before making a decision.

A Fraudulent Official Arrested and Detained. Zhu Ruixiang, a villager from Gedaiqiao Township in the 14th district of the county, is quite wealthy. His wife is addicted to opium. A member of the Zhu clan sent a letter to Jiang Yaoxian and Liu Zhiheng, two gun repairmen from the Huaiyin Military Command, to extort money. After receiving the letter, Jiang and others forged an official document from the Civil Affairs Department and went to Zhu Ruixiang's home to extort money. They found opium lamps and tools, but Zhu's wife was very clever and sat on the chamber pot urinating and would not get up, so they could not take her away and could not extort money. Zhu's tenant farmer, A, had a quarrel with Jiang and others, followed by a fight. Villagers gathered after hearing the news and reported to the water patrol team stationed in the township, who arrested Jiang and others and brought them to the city. The County Public Security Bureau transferred them to the County Court, where Prosecutor Zhu opened a court session and ordered them to be detained for review. Zhu has now fled without a trace, and the original letter to Jiang and others was submitted by Jiang and others to the County Court for review.

County Magistrate Peng Exposes a Case of Sexual Deprivation. At the Luxiangzhou Oil Mill on the west bank of the Puhui Bridge outside the north gate, the second son of Lu Xiangzhou, Jin Sheng, who suffers from tuberculosis, sucked the semen of an apprentice, Wu Jinshu. On the 20th, County Magistrate Peng heard about this and filed a judicial accusation. He ordered the bailiffs to bring Lu Xiangzhou and his son to court. County Magistrate Peng and Investigating Member Wu Chengshen interrogated them. Wu Mingxi Files Another Appeal. Wu Mingxi, a farmer from Dongtai County, was involved in a dispute with his neighbor, Wang, over farmland, which led to two charges of injury, intimidation, and fraud. He was sued by the Dongtai County Government, and after the trial, he was sentenced to five years in prison. Wu refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Zhenjiang Court. After repeated trials, Judge Zhong of the Criminal Court brought Wu to court for questioning yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. He immediately announced the Dongtai County Government's verdict was overturned, and Wu Mingxi was sentenced to one year in prison for the crime of injury and two years in prison for the crime of intimidation and fraud, with a combined sentence of three years in prison. The number of days of detention will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days. After the verdict, Wu still declared that he was not satisfied and would file another appeal.

Letter from the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Management Committee

Dear Sir,

We were very surprised to read in your newspaper about the explosion of the boiler of a Tianjin-Pukou passenger train. Upon investigation, on June 18, a northbound coal train of this line, with locomotive number 203, was traveling between Zhangbaling and Sanjie when the water inlet and steam pipe cover of the locomotive was blown off by steam, scalding the driver and fireman. Locomotive number 33 was dispatched to pull the train back to Zhangbaling. There was no explosion of the boiler of a passenger train. We believe that the news in your newspaper is inaccurate. We are writing to request that you investigate and correct the report. We hope for your prompt attention.

Sincerely,

Tianjin-Pukou Railway Management Committee

Local News

Customs Notice Regarding Territorial Sea Boundaries

The Jianghai Customs announces:

Regarding the matter of joint promulgation, the Ministry of Finance has ordered that, for the purpose of protecting tax revenue, the Executive Yuan has decreed that the boundaries of the territorial sea shall be defined as 12 nautical miles outwards from the low-tide mark on the coastline, as the area where Customs shall exercise all its maritime anti-smuggling powers. All merchants are hereby notified to comply. This notice is hereby promulgated.

June 20th, 20th year of the Republic of China.

Supervisor Tang Hai'an, Customs Commissioner Luo Fude.

Shanghai County Third Session

Second Day of the Delegate Assembly

Morning: Administrative Work Reports by the County Government and Various Bureaus

Afternoon: Discussion of Proposals to the Assembly Begins at 1 PM

The Third Delegate Assembly of Shanghai County, which commenced on the 20th at the County Party Headquarters, held its second day of continued meetings yesterday. The morning session was dedicated to administrative work reports by the County Government and various bureaus. The presidium consisted of Jiang Yanqiu, Xu Pengcheng, and Niu Changlian. Starting at 1 PM in the afternoon, the assembly continued discussing proposals. A detailed account of the various events is recorded below:

Attendees: Provincial Guiding Officer Chen Kanghe, Presidium members Jiang Yanqiu, Xu Pengcheng, and Niu Changlian, Delegates Zhang Yi, Jin Lemin, Huang Xingrang, Ding Borong, Li Youtian, Xu Pengcheng, Sun Jiafeng, Qiao Jiyuan, Zhang Jingye, Shen Hanqing, Wang Chengyao, Zhou Yuanliang, Kang Qiang, Jin Yongxin, Guo Xiangyuan, Peng Liren, Niu Changlian, Hu Naiwen, Shen Jing. In attendance: County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, Education Bureau Chief Shi She, Finance Bureau Chief Wang Li, Construction Bureau Chief Wu Wenhua, County Property Management Office Wu Jincheng, and others.

Telegram to the Provincial Party Headquarters: After the election of executive and supervisory committee members at the first official meeting the previous day, a telegram was immediately sent to the Provincial Party Headquarters, stating, "To the Zhenjiang Provincial Party Headquarters: The Third County Delegate Assembly of Shanghai was held on the morning of the 20th, following the opening ceremony, a preparatory meeting was convened, and executive and supervisory committee members were elected in the afternoon. The elected candidates for the Executive Committee are Jin Yongxin, Peng Liren, Lü Zhe, Kang Qiang, Gu Yunru, Shen Jing, Sun Zhongji, Sun Jianjun, Zhang Jingye, Zhang Yi, and others, totaling ten individuals. The candidates for the Supervisory Committee are Jiang Yanqiu, Wu Jingqing, Li Youtian, Shi She, and others, totaling four individuals. We are sending this telegram in advance to inform you; details will follow." Shanghai County Delegate Assembly Secretariat.

Yan Shenyu Reports: County Magistrate and Public Safety Bureau Chief Yan Shenyu reported, stating, in brief, that today's agenda included administrative work reports from the County Government and various bureaus. Regarding an overview of past work, in addition to a detailed written report, he would provide a brief report on the progress of various tasks over the past year. The County Government's work on autonomy matters included four key initiatives underway: (1) Citizen Oath: Statistics on registered citizens who have taken the oath in various districts, townships, and towns show 2,521 individuals in the first district, 14,799 in the second district, 2,335 in the third district, 11,168 in the fourth district, 1,413 in the fifth district, and 699 in the sixth district. (2) Township and Town Elections: The first and sixth districts have already completed these elections, while other districts are working to complete them as soon as possible. (3) Household Census: Actively underway. (4) Personnel Registration: He hoped that the heads of various townships and towns would dedicate their efforts to achieve perfection and thoroughness. Regarding the work of cleaning up the countryside, including (1) household registration, (2) collective guarantees, (3) inspection of firearms, (4) inspection of ships, (5) reorganization of the defense corps, and (6) armed patrols, all these tasks were being implemented effectively and systematically. He also provided a supplementary report on public safety administration, stating, in brief, that the county's public safety funds were originally designated from house taxes, which relied heavily on revenues from the urban area. After the separation of the county and city, the urban area fell under the city's jurisdiction, and the county's public safety funds were completely depleted. During the provincial and municipal division of governance conference, the situation was considered, and it was resolved to allocate 3,921 yuan per month from the city to the county's funds, according to the original budget. This was implemented accordingly. However, due to disputes over fund allocations between the province and the city, the municipal government suspended the subsidy in June of the 18th year. Starting from July of the previous year, the municipal government allowed a monthly allocation of half the amount. From April of this year, the municipal government has been able to allocate public safety funds as planned, which allows them to barely maintain operations. However, the total accumulated arrears amounted to approximately 17,000 yuan, making distribution a difficult issue. Regarding the rectification plan: (1) reducing the administrative expenses of the main bureau, (2) establishing a branch bureau in each district, (3) supplementing the required number of patrol officers with the dismissed members of the defense corps, and (4) supplementing firearms and uniforms. Detailed plans for all of these have been carefully prepared and submitted to the province for approval. The organization of the defense corps and the training of police officers are also being actively prepared, and so on.

The Finance Bureau's main tasks for the 19th year can be divided into (1) handling collection matters, (2) handling miscellaneous tax matters, (3) handling land registration matters, (4) handling public bond solicitation matters, (5) handling business tax matters, and (6) collecting local funds. He also hoped that all delegates would cooperate in assisting with local collection matters.

County Finance Bureau Urges Business Owners to Pay Supplementary Grain Tax

County Finance Bureau Urges Business Owners to Pay Supplementary Grain Tax

The Finance Bureau of Shanghai County Government previously received an order from the Finance Department of the Provincial Government of Jiangsu to investigate and process the case of Jiangsu Province's supplementary grain tax for land with no grain or barren land, with a deadline of six months for completion. Because business owners were observing and not reporting, Bureau Chief Wang Li has formulated an active plan, requiring all owners, regardless of whether the land is ripe or not, to come to the Bureau to report themselves within one month. Failure to report within the deadline will be regarded as the business owner abandoning property rights, and tenant farmers will be allowed to report and receive the land, with certification from the village scribe, pay the price according to regulations, and be issued an official deed to manage the property. Yesterday, the Finance Bureau notified each scribe to inform each business owner to report quickly and not to wait and delay themselves. Therefore, each business owner rushed to the Finance Bureau to report and pay the supplementary grain tax to protect their property rights.

French Concession Taxpayers' Association

Notice on Implementing the New System of Weights and Measures

The French Concession Taxpayers' Association issued a notice yesterday to residents of the concession, advising them to implement the new system of weights and measures. The notice states: "Regarding the promotion of the new system of weights and measures in this city, this Bureau has repeatedly convened meetings with the authorities of the Special District for coordination and discussion, and has also sent personnel to attend. The deadline for completing the unification by July 1 of this year is approaching. Each vegetable market has been scheduled to first implement the new system starting from June 1. The Special District is related to the observation of both Chinese and foreigners and should consistently promote it to establish a good reputation. Knowing that your association is the representative of the citizens, you are particularly enthusiastic about supervising the administration of the Special District and promoting improvements. We hereby send you this letter and hope that you will assist us in actively publicizing the necessity of unifying weights and measures, so that it can be completed on schedule. We will be very grateful." It is a need of the people since the founding of the Republic of China to unify the system of weights and measures. The National Government promulgated the Weights and Measures Law on February 16 of the 18th year for thorough unification and the Ministry of Industry stipulated that the implementation date for this city is on record. All people residing within the territory of the Republic of China should abide by and follow it. Those who violate this law will be punished according to law. As the old system of weights and measures has been legally abolished, anyone who uses it again is committing a criminal act. Therefore, we hereby notify residents of the concession that they should immediately comply with the new Weights and Measures Law, and all rulers, measuring containers, scales, etc., should be discarded and replaced with new ones as soon as possible. Legal rulers, measuring containers, scales, etc., can be purchased from the Weights and Measures Verification Office on Xieqiao Manufacturing Bureau Road. Please do not hesitate or delay to your own detriment. This is a notice.

Deadline for Jianghai Customs Manifests and Passports

Deadline: Before March 26

Jianghai Customs Commissioner Luo Fude issued a proclamation yesterday, stating: "Notice: It has been found that some merchants who previously submitted deposits to Jianghai Customs to report the transport of goods have not yet submitted the manifest or passport to the Customs for verification. Just Returned from the United States

Overseas Chinese Liu Guozhan Talks About National Salvation Through Vocational Skills

Welcoming Hu Hanmin to the United States

Hoping for Eternal Peace in the Country

Mr. Liu Guozhan, a member of the former Chinese United League who followed Sun Yat-sen in the Americas for revolutionary activities, has resigned from his position as Executive Committee Member of the Chinese Kuomintang General Branch in the United States due to his return to China to visit relatives. He arrived in Shanghai a few days ago. A reporter from the New Voice Society happened to meet him at his hotel yesterday and asked him about the feelings of overseas Chinese in the Americas regarding Mr. Hu Hanmin's trip to the United States and the recent situation in China. According to him, since Mr. Hu resigned, the Kuomintang General Branch in the Americas has sent telegrams to Beijing to retain him. Regarding Mr. Hu's convalescence in Nanjing and his resignation, more than a dozen telegrams have been exchanged between the Central Government and Mr. Hu himself. Overseas Chinese in the New World welcome Mr. Hu's trip to the United States. Before I left the United States, overseas Chinese even telegraphed Mr. Hu and the Central Government, urging him to go to the United States. However, Mr. Hu was unable to realize it at that time because his health had not yet recovered. Recently, it has been reported that Mr. Hu has recovered and that he himself has also expressed his intention to go to the United States, which may be realized in the future. As for the Guangdong Incident, when it first started, overseas Chinese in the Americas did not express much. Later, it was heard that the Guangdong side was actually in contact with Wang Jingwei and Zhang Fakui, and overseas Chinese in the Americas were quite displeased with this. Moreover, in view of the years of civil war, the use of force in the country is quite repulsive, so they hope for peace in the country and do not want any more wars. Furthermore, Member Lin Sen arrived in San Francisco on the 6th of this month, but I left the United States in May and did not meet Mr. Lin in San Francisco.

Du Chongyuan Speaks on National Salvation Through Vocational Skills

The Shanghai Vocational Skills Mutual Aid Society held its first lecture meeting yesterday afternoon at 3 PM at the Beiletang Hall of the Chinese Vocational Education Society. Mr. Du Chongyuan, a leading figure in the industrial circles of the Northeast and a representative of Liaoning at the National Conference, was invited to speak. He was inspired by the success story of Japanese entrepreneur An'nosuke Zenshiro, who built his business from scratch. His success story is most worthy of emulation. Our country is under the economic invasion of the great powers. If we do not be practical and bury ourselves in our work, but only engage in empty talk, how can the country last long? He also cited Gandhi's adherence to the non-cooperation policy as evidence of working hard.

And our association members must be the first to eliminate this morning's food. We await clear instructions. This is a declaration."

Reasons for Rising Rice Prices

Someone is Collecting and Transporting for Export

Recently, rice prices in both the northern and southern rice markets in Shanghai have gradually increased due to the shortage of sources. Yesterday, the highest price of white japonica rice sold in the northern market was 14.8 yuan per stone, then 14.6 yuan, then 14.2 yuan. Thin japonica rice was 13.7 yuan per stone, then 13.5 yuan, and white yuan rice was 13.4 yuan per stone, which was an increase of 23 yuan compared to last week. According to people in the rice industry, the reason for the recent increase in rice prices is that someone is secretly collecting rice in Changshu and Xixiang and transporting it for export in large quantities, which has caused the inventory in various villages to be almost exhausted. Therefore, the sources in Shanghai are becoming scarce, and in a blink of an eye, there will be a shortage of rice, and prices may continue to rise.

Zhejiang Province

Summer Cocoons Will Be Affected by the Weather Again

Zhejiang has always been a famous silkworm area in our country. The cocoon season is earlier than that of Jiangsu. This year's spring cocoons were severely damaged by the weather, and the cocoon production was extremely poor, with only 30% of the harvest. In recent years, the silk factories in Hangzhou, Shaoxing, Huzhou, and Jiaxing in Zhejiang Province have been developing rapidly. The number of silk factories in the province has reached more than 20, and the demand for dry cocoon raw materials has increased sharply. The spring cocoons of each province this year totaled 123,000 dan, and 70-80% of them were purchased by silk merchants in Shanghai and residual cocoon merchants. The amount received by the province's silk factories is limited and cannot meet the demand. Various manufacturers, such as Weicheng, have to encourage farmers to raise summer cocoons to make up for the lack of spring cocoons. Therefore, this summer, cocoon farmers in each province are hatching summer silkworms early, and the amount of feeding is not weak. After receiving the ants, the weather is sunny and warm, which is very suitable for raising silkworms. After the first sleep, the silkworm ants developed smoothly and the feeding was good. The feed (that is, summer mulberry leaves) is sufficient, and there is hope for a good harvest. Currently, the early batches in Hangzhou and Shaoxing are about to enter the fourth sleep, and the late batches are in the third sleep. Jiaxing, Huzhou and other places are also in the second sleep. However, in the past few days, there has been continuous mold rain, followed by sultry heat and sudden cold, which has caused changes in the early batch of silkworm ants. They stopped sleeping and eating, and due to the influence of eating wet leaves and uneven temperature, they leaked yellow and spewed black, resulting in stiffness and death, almost repeating the mistakes of the spring silkworms. The current situation is not good. Although the weather has turned sunny recently, the climate is still cold, and the future of summer silkworms is still difficult to be optimistic.

Bean and Rice Company

Exemption from Business Tax for Paid Posts

The Business Tax Preparatory Office of the Municipal Finance Bureau sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "Regarding your Chamber's official letter stating that the bean and rice businesses in this city have been paying teeth tax and therefore should not be required to pay business tax again, but the current business tax regulations in this city include the grain industry, causing concerns among the relevant trade associations, requesting an interpretation for dissemination, etc. Upon review, the draft business tax rate schedule for this city specifies that the grain industry refers specifically to those engaged in the sale of grain. For businesses that act as agents for buying and selling, merchants holding dental posts should refer to Article 20 of the draft business tax regulations of this city, change the name to business tax, and continue to collect taxes according to the old tax rate. The current tax rate is not inclusive. Due to the reasons mentioned above, we are responding for your information and dissemination."

Various Businesses in Wusong

Yesterday's Debt Collection from the Chamber of Commerce Ended Without Result

A Petition Will Be Filed with Relevant Authorities in Beijing and Shanghai

The Social Affairs Bureau, the Public Security Bureau, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent personnel to Wusong the day before yesterday to take over the Wusong Chamber of Commerce, as detailed in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that various businesses in Wusong claim that the Chamber of Commerce borrowed large sums of money from them during previous war disasters to supply military needs, accumulating debts of over 10,000 yuan. The creditors, concerned that the receiving authorities have not yet expressed any intention to address the debt issue and might simply ignore it, went to the private residences of former executive committee members Zheng Shushan, Zhang Yuchi, and Yang Yuankang yesterday to demand answers. Unable to handle the incessant demands, Zheng and others asked them to come to the Chamber of Commerce at 8 p.m. to discuss the matter. However, when the time came, over a hundred people gathered at the Chamber of Commerce, their demeanor fierce and voices loud, almost resorting to violence against Zheng and others. Fearing the outbreak of trouble, Zheng and others immediately telegraphed the First Precinct of the Seventh District of the Public Security Bureau for protection. Upon receiving the message, the precinct immediately dispatched several armed police officers to dissuade the debt collectors from causing a disturbance and to wait patiently for a resolution, fortunately averting any disaster. Subsequently, the creditors elected representatives on the spot and plan to go to the relevant authorities in Beijing and Shanghai to petition in the coming days.

Guo Waifeng Discusses the Current Situation of the China Merchants Bureau

Guo Waifeng, the newly appointed Director-General of the China Merchants Bureau, has been in office for over a month. Yesterday, a reporter from the Daily News visited Guo at his private residence to inquire about the recent situation of the China Merchants Bureau and its reorganization plans. Guo provided detailed answers, which are summarized below:

The Jinliyuan Case Regarding the Jinliyuan Wharf case, the French side's attitude remains very firm. However, after direct negotiations with the Bureau, there has been some progress. French Consul-General Geng Ge-lin stated that 300,000 yuan is required for redemption, while the Bureau is currently offering 250,000 yuan, which is close. The China Merchants Bureau has sought opinions from the government and business community. A final decision will be made based on the extent of the French side's concessions. A resolution is expected soon.

Return of Rented Ships The General Headquarters had rented nine Yangtze River ships from the Bureau to transport troops. The Bureau currently has only two ships left. Guo Waifeng went to Beijing to request the return of the ships. The General Headquarters has agreed to return them gradually. Recently, the Jianghua ship was returned first.

Demolition of Properties The Bureau owns several valuable properties on Sichuan Road. Recently, they were demolished due to their dilapidated condition. Since the properties have already been mortgaged, no new buildings will be constructed unless external investors invest in building them.

Reorganization Plan Guo also told the reporter from the Daily News that the China Merchants Bureau is in a state of disrepair with countless problems. Talking about reorganization is like discussing the Twenty-Four Histories, not knowing where to start. Generally speaking, it is necessary to start with small matters. At the same time, it is also necessary to reorganize the finances first. Once the finances are in order, all difficulties can be solved easily. The most pressing issue is that the ships have been in service for a long time and are in a state of disrepair, but there are no funds to build new ships. Allowing the old ships to be phased out indefinitely is not a long-term solution. Therefore, it is urgent to reorganize the finances to build new ships to facilitate shipping.

Postponement of Layoffs The reporter also inquired about the rumored layoffs. Guo replied that although layoffs are a way to save money, there are other issues that are more important than layoffs. The layoff issue must be postponed for now. Currently, there are too many employees in the Bureau. In principle, if an organization has too many employees, they should be laid off; if it is understaffed, employees should be added. He also agrees with this principle. However, the China Merchants Bureau is not yet at the stage where layoffs are necessary.

After the leave expires, it is hoped that you will quickly assume your new position, fulfilling the expectations placed upon you. Special reply. Executive Yuan."

Exchange of Documents and Telegrams Regarding the Qu Case

The following is a compilation of the recent letter from the Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association to the Shanghai Municipal Government and the reply from the Shanghai Bar Association of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the case of Qu Shixiang and Ma Ruixiang being stabbed by American sailors: (1) (Omitted above) Regarding the case of American sailors stabbing Qu Shixiang and Ma Ruixiang, our Association previously telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to file a serious protest and sent a letter to the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to handle the matter. We then received a telegram from Qi of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stating that the case had been referred to the Shanghai Municipal Government for investigation and reply, and that it would be handled upon receipt of the reply. We also received a reply from the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on June 2 stating that the case involves local negotiations and has been stipulated to be handled by the Municipal Government. This is to present the case to Your Excellency for handling and filing a serious protest with the American authorities. Currently, Lawyer Wu Jingxiong, introduced by the Shanghai Bar Association, is representing our Association in handling this case. We request Your Excellency to preside over the progress to safeguard national rights. We have sent Mr. Peng Yangwu to deliver the letter. We hope that you will grant an audience to clarify the negotiation strategy and to comfort the hopes of the people and their families. Sincerely, the Shanghai Municipal Government. (2) (Omitted above) Regarding the case of American sailors stabbing Qu and Ma, Mr. Peng, a member of our Association, delivered a letter on the 15th of this month, requesting Your Excellency to preside over the negotiations to safeguard national rights. Secretary Guo granted an audience and instructed us to prepare detailed notes and submit written evidence for verification. We have recorded the notes of this case separately for your review and attached two photos. The bloody clothes are still kept by the injured parties' families and can be produced for verification at any time. On behalf of the injured parties, we request Your Excellency to propose a serious protest to achieve the dual objectives of punishing the murderers and compensating for the losses, and to ensure the safety of Chinese people in the concession in the future. We are waiting for your orders. (3) The Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association has reviewed the case of Qu Shixiang, etc., being stabbed by American sailors. On June 8, a telegram was sent stating that the Shanghai Municipal Government had replied that the Public Security Bureau had been ordered to investigate and reply with the English names of the offending sailors. The reply will be communicated upon arrival, etc. In this case, the English names of the American sailors, the diagnosis from the hospital, and other evidence that can prove the American sailors' atrocities are all important and should be investigated and reported separately by the Association for negotiations with the American Ambassador. (4) To whom it may concern, the letter states that Qu Shixiang, etc., were stabbed by American sailors and requests the Association to uphold justice and recommend a lawyer familiar with American law to study the progress plan. Upon being submitted to the 81st Executive Supervisory Committee meeting of the Association, it was resolved to recommend member Wu Jingxiong as a volunteer to assist in this case. In addition to the Association sending a letter to member Wu for handling, this letter is sent to your Association for your information and to inform the original reporter to go to the Wu Jingxiong Law Firm at Jing'an Villa, Weihaiwei Road, for a face-to-face consultation. All the procedures for the progress of this case can be guided. To the Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association. (5) The Shanghai Municipal Party Department's reply, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's reply to the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession, and the Shanghai Committee of All Circles Opposing the Atrocities of American Sailors' public letter are all omitted.

Baoshan Regulations

Rickshaw Rental and Fare Prices

The Baoshan Construction Bureau, finding that there were no regulations for rickshaw rental and fare prices in the county, ordered the Transportation Affairs Office to formulate a simple price list according to local conditions. The list was submitted to the county government by the Bureau and passed at the 49th County Administration Meeting. It was then forwarded to the Provincial Department for record. Upon receiving instructions from the Jiangsu Construction Department to comply and implement, Director Wu of the Bureau, in addition to complying with the order to announce it on June 15 and reporting it to the County Government and sub-district police stations, also issued a notice to the people of the county to make them aware. The rickshaw rental and fare price list stipulated in Baoshan is recorded as follows: (A) The maximum rickshaw rental price is four yuan per month. Vehicle repair costs are borne by the rickshaw owner, and rickshaw taxes are borne by the rickshaw puller. (B) Rickshaw fares are as follows: Between Chengzhi and Taiwan Fort, a distance of 2.7 kilometers, 20 cents per trip; between Chengzhi and Wusong, 3.35 kilometers, 25 cents per trip; between Chengzhi and Sanguantang, 2 kilometers, 15 cents per trip; between Chengzhi and Yanghang, 6.4 kilometers, 40 cents per trip; between Yanghang and Wusong, 7 kilometers, 40 cents per trip; between Yanghang and Gujia Town, 5.5 kilometers, 40 cents per trip; between Yanghang and Liuhang, 6.8 kilometers, 40 cents per trip; between Dachang and Xinzha, 7 kilometers, 30 cents per trip; between Dachang and Pengpu, 4 kilometers, 20 cents per trip; between Dachang and Jiangwan, 5.2 kilometers, 30 cents per trip; between Dachang and Tangqiao, 4.9 kilometers, 30 cents per trip; between Dachang and Gujia Town, 6.2 kilometers, 35 cents per trip; between Dachang and Liuhang, 9 kilometers, 45 cents per trip; between Liuhang and Gujia Town, 2.9 kilometers, 15 cents per trip; between Luodian and Jiading, 9.2 kilometers, 50 cents per trip; between Luodian and Shi Xianggong Temple, 2.6 kilometers, 20 cents per trip; between Luodian and Liuhang, 6.7 kilometers, 35 cents per trip; between Luodian and Panjia Bridge, 5 kilometers, 30 cents per trip; between Luodian and Shugong Bridge, 10.8 kilometers, 55 cents per trip; between Luodian and Liuhe, 14.2 kilometers, 70 cents per trip. The hourly rate for chartered rickshaws is 20 cents. (All prices are in small yuan.)

Zhang Shiming's Concubine Appeals

Accepted by the High Court Second Branch

Trial to Open Soon

Zhou Miaoying, the divorced concubine of the late Nanxun wealthy merchant Zhang Shiming, filed a lawsuit last year against Zhang's wife, Xu, and Qu, her biological son, because the latter was married without her consent, requesting confirmation of their mother-son relationship. Xu and others hired lawyers Zhu Sifu and Jiang Yiping, presenting a contract signed by Zhou in the past, severing her family relationship with the Zhang family, proving that she had no right to interfere in the Zhang family's affairs. Zhou lost the case. Still unwilling to accept the outcome, she appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. It is now learned that the case has been accepted by the High Court Second Branch, which has issued summonses, delivered to both parties, and notified the two lawyers, to appear in court for trial soon.

Conditions for a Concubine's Divorce

Sassoon Comprador Shen Yanling

Separates from Beloved Concubine

Gives 50,000 Yuan in Alimony

Shen Yanling, currently the comprador of the British company New Sassoon, is the son of the late Sassoon Ah Si. Originally from Dongting Mountain, he inherited his father's position as the comprador of the company. He owns millions of assets and is one of the wealthy merchants in Shanghai, residing in Fengjili, Nanjing Road. His mistress, Cheng Yuzhen, resides at 15 Jiufu Lane, Mengdelan Road, Xinzha. Originally a woman of the demimonde, Cheng was hired by Shen when she was only fifteen. Soon after, she gave birth to a son. Not only did Shen dote on her, but the first wife also favored her, so when the son was an infant, the first wife took him to raise as her own. Later, Cheng gave birth to two more sons. Now the eldest son is six years old, the second son is five years old, and the youngest is two years old. In the blink of an eye, Cheng has been with Shen for nine years. Every month, Shen would provide her with generous living expenses without interruption. However, as the saying goes, the moon waxes and wanes, and those who gather for a long time must part. Recently, Shen's attitude towards Cheng has changed drastically. He used to love her in every possible way, but now he hates her beyond measure. He no longer wants to see her and has cut off her support, causing Cheng and her children to fear that they will have no rice to cook. Unable to continue, she did not know what to do. She asked people to persuade him, but it was all in vain. Even if the concubine's heart is like silk, the man's heart is like iron. She knew that the fate was over and they had to separate, so she asked lawyer Zhu Sifu to represent her and negotiate with Shen. After repeated exchanges of letters and consultations, three conditions were decided: (1) The two parties sever their relationship as husband and concubine. (2) Shen Yanling pays Cheng Yuzhen 50,000 yuan. (3) The three sons born to Cheng Yuzhen are all taken by Shen Yanling to raise. The agreement was officially signed a few days ago, and from then on, they will be strangers. It is said that Cheng is still young and beautiful. Although she owns a large sum of money, she cannot bear the loneliness. She plans to re-enter the entertainment industry, playing the pipa again. If she meets her former lover at a banquet in the future, how will they feel when they look back on the past?

Shanghai Bank

News of the Proportional Distribution of Debt Funds

Since the 18th of this month, the Baxianqiao branch of Shanghai Bank has begun to proportionally distribute the debt funds of the affiliated Riyue Bank and Dashijie Amusement Department under the Gongfa Company. On the first day, after 7 o'clock, the entrance of the bank was already crowded with people. It was raining heavily, so the bank opened its doors early at 8 o'clock to facilitate the creditors. By 4 o'clock in the afternoon, there were still about 100 people waiting to receive their funds. The bank specially extended its office hours by two hours. The bank also opened early at 8 o'clock on the second day. There were even more people on this day than on the first day. During the two days, the bank sent more than 10 staff members to issue funds and take care of everything, without a moment's rest throughout the day. They ate bread for lunch. The third day was the abolished Lunar Dragon Boat Festival, and the Shanghai banking and money industries were all closed. Yesterday was the birth anniversary, and the bank was open all day as usual, showing a commendable spirit of service. It is said that 594 households were paid on the first day, totaling 19,351.39 yuan; 645 households were paid on the second day, totaling 18,806.70 yuan; 487 households were paid on the third day, totaling 13,352.80 yuan; and 519 households were paid on the fourth day, totaling 13,820.97 yuan. In addition, the liquidation office opened checks for the Baxianqiao branch to be distributed by lawyers on behalf of the creditors, totaling more than 140,000 yuan.

Wei Min Attempts Suicide by Taking Medicine

The Man Who Killed His Wife and Son Last Year

Now Takes a Large Dose of Tranquilizers

On the evening of the 17th of this month, a traveler came to the Wugong Hotel at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Shilu Road, claiming to be surnamed Ren, given name Wei, and from Beiping to Shanghai, about 30 years old. He opened room 436 and lived there. At first, he lived a secluded life, closing the door and sitting alone, rarely calling the room service. Yesterday morning, Ren went out alone, returning and leaving several times. Around 6 p.m., he was alone in the room, burying his head in writing, then closing the door tightly without a sound. The room service staff suspected the guest's behavior, so they paid close attention to his every move. Seeing that he was alone and closed the door tightly without a sound, they reported it to the front desk. After about two hours, he still had not opened the door, fearing that something might have happened, the front desk staff broke the ventilation skylight and looked inside, seeing Ren lying on the bed, seemingly asleep, but his face was pale and his condition was not good. So they broke open the door and went inside to see the real situation. The so-called Ren Wei was lying on the bed, unable to be moved, and did not respond when called. There was a suicide note on the table, and medicine bottles were also found. They immediately telephoned the police, who sent an ambulance to take Ren to Renji Hospital for treatment. At the time, he was wearing a Zhongshan suit and was extremely depressed, but he was still breathing, and his condition was very dangerous. Later, it was investigated that this suicide attempter was Wei Min, also known as Yan Can, who had caused a sensation last autumn, having pushed his wife and children into the river to die. The court sentenced him to one year in prison for inciting suicide. Wei is now 33 years old, from Henan, and has served as a county magistrate and police chief. This suicide attempt was probably due to environmental pressure and the inability to recover, so he took this drastic measure. Before committing suicide, he wrote several letters, one to the hotel manager, saying that he had no choice but to take this action, hoping that he would be buried with his wife and children in the public cemetery after his death. Ren paid 10 yuan for the room when he arrived at the hotel, so he also mentioned it in the suicide note, saying that if it was not enough, there were still silver yuan in his small bag. Wei swallowed a large amount of tranquilizers, and his life is in danger.

A Record of the Annual Banquet of the Shanghai University Alumni Association

The Shanghai University Alumni Association held a banquet at the Xin Xin Restaurant to celebrate the graduation of this year's male and female students. Over 200 people attended, including over 40 male and female graduates, the school's president, faculty, and alumni. The banquet began at 7:30 p.m. with a speech by Mr. Yu Bingyong, the president of the Alumni Association, followed by a piano solo by Ms. Li Xianmin, the performance of Chinese music by the Shanghai University Chinese Music Society, and the singing of the school song by all attendees. Vice Minister Zhao of the Ministry of Industry gave a speech, stating that university students have the responsibility to lead the masses. According to recent statistics, there is only one university graduate for every 20,000 people in our country, which means that each university student must lead 20,000 people. Looking back at the current trend in our country, everything is being Westernized, with Western food, Western clothing, and even strange things happening due to the prevalence of dancing, while the essence of our country is being rejected, causing great unrest throughout the country. He hoped that Shanghai University students would lead the masses on the path to light, and that the Alumni Association would have a sense of connection, gather wisdom, and encourage each other. He hoped that they would pay special attention to this. Mr. Xu Zhendong's humorous performance was extremely funny, causing laughter throughout the hall. Former President Wei gave a speech, urging the students to pay attention to the spirit of Shanghai University and not let it decline. He said that Shanghai University is now increasingly on the path of preserving the essence of our country. Later, Ms. Qiu Yufeng, the leader of the class of 1920, gave a reply. The banquet ended with a chorus, a humorous play, and a raffle.

Obituary of Silas Aaron Hardoon

Silas Aaron Hardoon passed away a few days ago. As previously reported, Hardoon, adhering to Jewish customs, was immediately buried in his new garden cemetery after the grand funeral. The location is bounded by Xijie Qian Yuan to the west, connected to Canglang Pavilion to the east, near Shuixin Cottage to the south, and belongs to Tianyan Realm to the north, covering an area of approximately twenty acres. On the morning of the 11th, Jewish Bishop Yifeng, along with fellow believers, performed a baptism ceremony, followed by the encoffining. Around 9:00 AM, the coffin was placed in the hall, where the bishop chanted scriptures for a long time. Three to four hundred male and female believers attended. As soon as the chanting stopped, the believers carried the coffin bottom and escorted it out to the burial site. The grave had already been dug and prepared. No fewer than a thousand guests from various circles held the ropes and respectfully escorted the coffin into the tomb. The believers personally completed the soil covering. Over a hundred wreaths were placed and arranged. The tasks of planting trees and other matters will be handled in sequence. After the burial ceremony, a mourning hall was set up in Yanyutang, where all staff members of Hardoon & Co. and the entire staff of Aili Garden offered sacrifices to express their sorrow and respect. For this funeral arrangement, Miss Juemi was in charge of the office. Accountants, clerks, general affairs personnel, and other staff were assigned from the original employees of the garden and from the Pinghang staff. Those who accepted the invitations were all employees of the company, former employees, former students, and several close friends of Miss Juemi. Since the order had been predetermined, things proceeded smoothly. It is said that a memorial service will be held within the next five weeks.

Rumor of a Two-Headed Child

Hundreds Deceived

Turns Out to Be a Tumor

The wife of An Maolin, a villager from Xujiazhaicun, Zhanghuabang, Wusong, gave birth to a girl at around 11:00 AM yesterday. This child had a huge tumor on the back of her neck, as large as her head. Her limbs were like those of a normal person. Initially, it was thought to be a child with two heads, which was considered very strange. However, after birth, she did not cry and seemed to be ill. Since her mother was poor and ill, she planned to abandon the child in the wilderness, unwilling to raise her. She entrusted someone to take her to a grassland near the Guanshengyuan preserved plum advertisement sign on Zhou Tang, Yunzaobang South, Wusong. A passerby happened to see it and, at first glance, also thought it was a child born with two heads, which was very strange, and therefore abandoned. The news spread to Wusong, and soon it was rumored that a two-headed child had been discovered there. Some even mistakenly claimed that a monster with three heads and six arms had been found. The entire town was immediately in an uproar. Driven by curiosity, hundreds of people went to see it by sampan. The outer roads were as crowded as a tide, causing traffic congestion. General ferries tripled their profits. By 6:00 PM, more and more people were gathering to watch. Zhang, the chief of the first sub-district of the seventh district, learned of the matter. Concerned that the traffic congestion might cause trouble, he sent police officers and local security to summon the child's family to the station. Around 8:00 PM, An Maolin was summoned to the station. Chief Zhang instructed him to take the child back and raise her, otherwise abandoning her would be a crime. An immediately took the child back home, but she was already on her last breath and unlikely to survive.

Boy and Girl Bitten by Rabid Dog

Rabid Dog Shot Dead on the Spot by Police Officer

Gu Jinlai, a 15-year-old boy residing at No. 31 Beishizi Lane, went out to buy something at around 6:00 PM yesterday. While walking on Zijing Road, he was attacked by a rabid dog, which tore his right shoulder and bit his leg. He fell to the ground in agony. Shen Afu, a 9-year-old girl, was also bitten on the leg by the same rabid dog. Both fell to the ground in extreme pain. Police officer Shen Qiyun arrived and immediately shot and killed the rabid dog. He took the injured boy and girl to the Second District Sub-Bureau. After inspection by Director Xu, the boy Gu Jinlai's injuries were deemed more severe and he was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. The girl was taken home by her father for self-care.
