Smuggling Opium, Fined Three Thousand Yuan

Chen Ada smuggled 65 pounds of opium worth 3,500 yuan from another port to Shanghai on the 18th of this month. He hired a rickshaw. While passing through the French Concession, he was discovered by French police detectives Lu Jinchen and Mao Jinsheng, who arrested Chen along with the opium and took them to the police station. The other day, they were brought before the French court for investigation. The police chief reported the previous situation and presented the opium as evidence. Upon questioning, Chen Ada confessed to smuggling opium without denial. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced Chen to a fine of 3,000 yuan, and the opium was confiscated.

Kidnapper Handed Over to Suzhou for Trial

Yu Wang, a rural woman from Suzhou, had her seven-year-old daughter, Yu Xiaomei, kidnapped to Shanghai last month by Xu Jiang, a woman from the same village. Xu entrusted Zhou Li, Zhang Chen, and Cai Jinming to introduce her to Zhao Zhang, intending to sell her to Zhao. The matter was discovered by a French police detective, who arrested all the above persons, including Xu Sifa, the husband of the kidnapper Jiang. The other day, the plaintiff, Yu Wang, was summoned to the court, and the defendants were handed over to the criminal court of the French Concession for investigation. The plaintiff, Yu Wang, complained about the kidnapping of her daughter. When questioned, Xu Jiang claimed that Yu Xiaomei was entrusted to her by her mother to come to Shanghai to work as a domestic helper. The child was temporarily lodged with Zhou Li, a woman she knew, who was entrusted to sell her. She claimed she did not know the details. The others prevaricated in their statements. Zhou Li, Cai Jinming, Zhang Chen, and others all confessed that Xu Jiang had indeed entrusted them to find buyers. Zhao Zhang claimed that Cai and others had brought the girl, but she refused because her origins were unclear. Xu Sifa claimed that the girl was kidnapped by his wife and he was unaware of it. The Chinese and Western officials ordered Xu Jiang and Xu Sifa to be sent to the Wu County District Court for trial. Yu Xiaomei was taken away by her mother. The others were released.

Renovation of Nanjing Grand Theater Nearing Completion

Due to weather conditions, the Nanjing Grand Theater in this city was unable to complete the renovations to its satisfaction when it opened last year, so it temporarily suspended performances to rearrange the premises. During this time, it installed artificial air conditioning equipment to isolate sound, so that the theater would not have any noise when the air conditioning was turned on for performances. It is said that most of the above work has been completed and the public performance date is not far off. According to the theater's external announcement, dozens of blockbuster films have been selected and will be shown successively after the opening, so that those who come to the theater for cooling will have an unexpected visual feast.

Yang Brand Lubricating Oil Sells Well

The Yang Brand lubricating oil manufactured by the Anquan Company in Weianfang, Haining Road, has long been selling well throughout the country. Recently, it has been exclusively distributed by the various branch offices of the Hengfuzhong Watch Company. As gold prices have soared and costs have increased, the company, in order to benefit users, still sells it at the original price of 60 cents per bottle. As a result, direct mail orders to the company have been very enthusiastic recently.

Cheng Haitao Creates Five-Language Night School

Cheng Haitao, who is proficient in foreign literature, has now established a night school for five languages—English, French, German, Japanese, and Russian—at the mouth of Jiangyuan Alley. He has specially hired renowned female scholars from various countries to serve as professors, and emphasizes practical conversation, starting with crash courses to create practical talents in the shortest possible time. It is heard that the Japanese language course has already started and enrollment is very enthusiastic.

Rong Meiqing's Funeral Honors

Rong Meiqing was a prominent figure in Wuxi, a leader in the cotton yarn industry. He was generous and enthusiastic in promoting public welfare in his hometown, always taking the lead. Mr. Rong managed his business throughout his life, accumulating millions in wealth. He regarded money as something external and dedicated himself to benefiting the people. Although over forty years old, he was still concerned about not having an heir. Unexpectedly, he had a son at the age of knowing destiny, truly proving that heaven's rewards are unfailing. Mr. Rong was burdened with heavy business and traveled between Shanghai and Hankou for a long time. Over time, he became exhausted and fell ill, passing away at his residence in Hanyang the other day. The news of his death was met with widespread mourning. Yesterday, a memorial service was specially held at Chongfu Temple on Guling Road. Thousands of gentry, merchants, and people from all walks of life in Shanghai came to pay their respects. The funeral procession was adorned with plain carriages and white horses, reaching a peak of grandeur.

Carelessness on Beller Road Yesterday Morning

A fire broke out in the home of the Zhang family at No. 795 Sanyou Lane, Beller Road, French Concession, at around 1:00 AM yesterday morning due to carelessness. The flames soared and sparks flew everywhere, burning down two rooms and the furniture inside in an instant. It is said that the loss was around one thousand yuan. The fire was extinguished after the fire brigade arrived by car.

Crazy Man Lying Naked on Trolley Tracks

Female Spectators Embarrassed

At around 10:00 AM yesterday, a man suddenly appeared at the Youche Wharf in Nanshi and lay directly on the trolley tracks. In an instant, a crowd of onlookers gathered. The man was about forty years old, his eyes tightly closed, his face covered in mud, barely resembling a human face. He wore a white, short shirt on his upper body, but his lower body was completely naked, without shoes or socks. The spectators were amazed by this strange sight. Many women, embarrassed, turned their faces away. Li Shijie, the security guard of the 18th station, heard about the incident and arrived. Because there were so many onlookers, traffic was obstructed and the trolley was in danger of passing. He went forward and ordered the man to get up, but the man ignored him. Li had no choice but to drag him off the trolley tracks and take him to the First Sub-Bureau of the District. A large crowd followed along the way. After arriving at the station, the chief conducted a preliminary interrogation, asking the man his name and origin. The man did not say a word, staring blankly. He was diagnosed with mental illness and it was ordered that a written report be sent to the Municipal Police Bureau to request arrangements for accommodation and food.

Accusation Due to New Shoes and Socks

Shoe Store Suspects Theft

Illegally Uses Torture to Coerce a Confession

The Central Shoe Store at No. 788 North Sichuan Road had 57 yuan stolen from the cash drawer. All the store employees denied taking it. Later, it was noticed that Chen Yougen (also known as Xu Yougen), a Chongming native who delivered meals from Tongchang Restaurant at No. 423 Zhaopu Road, had new shoes and socks. The store suspected that Chen had stolen the money. Shen Hehai, a store employee, impersonated a detective and invited someone to take Chen to a secluded place, where he was privately tortured and beaten to force him to confess to the theft and write a confession. Zhou Caifa, Chen's employer, learned of the matter, reported the false accusation and illegal torture to the police station. The police sent detectives to arrest the shoe store owner Zhang Sansan and Shen Hehai, Zhou Qifa, Zhu Axiao, and others, and took them to the Special District Court for custody and investigation. The other day, the trial continued. Liu Xinsan, a fortune teller who wrote the confession, was summoned by the police to testify, stating that the confession was written by Zhang and Shen, stating that Chen Yougen had stolen 57 yuan and voluntarily admitted to compensation, deducting three yuan from his salary each month. Although Chen was also present at the time, he did not say a word. Zhang and others forced him to sign it, showing reluctance. Zhang denied entrusting Liu to write the confession. Judge Feng ordered Liu to identify the person, but Liu claimed that there were many onlookers next to the fortune-telling stall at the time, so he might have mistaken the person. Judge Feng interrogated the other defendants and ordered Zhang to pay a 500-yuan shop bond. The others were remanded in custody and a date was set for sentencing.

Young Widow Requests Alimony

Wu Tang, a young widow from Jiangwan, recently hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the District Court, requesting her father-in-law, Wu Mengtan (a Jiangwan municipal commissioner who also runs Derentang Pharmacy and an oil press in the town), to pay her 5,000 yuan in alimony. Her statement was as follows: She married the defendant's third son, Chuiwei, on March 17th of this year, but after only twenty days of marriage, Chuiwei passed away from illness on April 7th. Her husband was already ill when they married. Since her husband's death, she has been subjected to cold words and harsh treatment in the family, which she can no longer tolerate. She requests that the court grant her permission to live separately and award her alimony. The case has been tried repeatedly without a conclusion. The other day, Judge Ding Shikui held another hearing. Both parties attended with their lawyers. As a result of the trial, it was agreed that Wu Mengtan would subsidize Wu Tang with 25 yuan per month for living expenses for six months, and she would still live in her husband's house, with her meals provided by her father-in-law. Both parties were satisfied and a settlement was reached. The judge wrote a settlement record in court, stating that there should be no abuse, otherwise she would be allowed to live separately. Both parties signed and left the court.

Shanghai Wireless Telegraph Station of the Ministry of Communications

Establishment of a Recreation Organization

In order to provide proper recreation for all staff members of the Shanghai Wireless Telegraph Station of the Ministry of Communications during their spare time and to adjust their service spirit, they have initiated the organization of a recreation club, dividing it into ten groups: music, billiards, tennis, track and field, swimming, basketball, chess, volleyball, soccer, and martial arts. They have also invited renowned experts to provide guidance. It was officially established at the beginning of this month. It is heard that the staff of the club have already elected the honorary president as Zhu Qiqing, the managing engineer of the station; the president as Jin Dingguang; the vice president as Zhu Yangzhi; the executive officers as Zhang Jingfu and Xu Zongyi; the secretaries as Lu Huaiqing and Xu Tingliang; and the accountants as Xie Chunpu and Ji Huanlin. They have all taken office and are actively proceeding with activities. It is expected that the music, tennis, and basketball groups will be the most successful.

Recent News on the Miss World Bathing Beauty Pageant

The Miss World Bathing Beauty Pageant will be held this summer at the Ming Garden Swimming Pool. According to recent reports, the bathing beauty pageant will be held in two stages. The first stage is exclusively for foreign girls. The preliminary selection is scheduled for Saturday afternoon, July 25th. All participants must wear bathing suits. On August 8th, all must wear evening gowns. After two rigorous rounds of selection, they will be qualified for the final selection. The second stage is for Chinese girls. The dates are set for August 22nd and August 29th, also divided into bathing suit and evening gown categories. Eight beauties will be selected from each stage. A special beauty pageant judging panel will be formed to carefully select the winners. The final will be held on September 12th, with a grand banquet and public judging to determine who will be Miss Shanghai. The judges will be composed of renowned Chinese and Western gentry, merchants, and noblewomen from Shanghai. Most of the ticket revenue will be donated to charitable organizations in Shanghai. The elected Miss Shanghai will be awarded a large silver cup by the organizing committee to celebrate the grand occasion. The other elected beauties will also receive various precious gifts. The competition certificates have now been printed. Those who wish to join can obtain them from Guanglu Grand Theater, Dahua Open-Air Cinema, Central Stadium, the Ming Garden Office at No. 396 Jiangxi Road, or the Far East Entertainment Company at No. 6 Jiujiang Road. Fill in your name and send it to the Ming Garden Bathing Beauty Pageant Committee before July 18th.

This has been reported to the Municipal Government under Instruction No. 10523 for record-keeping." In addition to issuing separate orders, this instruction is hereby given for your information. Ye Xinan Begins Editing Lexicon

Ye Xinan, the inventor of the four-corner indexing method, has received numerous letters from all walks of life since soliciting opinions from various sectors. It is widely believed that this indexing method has genuine value, and Ye is urged to compile and print a dictionary as soon as possible to benefit the academic community. It is heard that, for the sake of caution, Ye is editing a lexicon while continuing to improve the method. At the same time, he is paying close attention to the collection of characters and the printing of phonetics and definitions. It is expected that the book will be completed in three years.

News from Various Hometown Associations

Jiangxi: The Jiangxi Shanghai Fellow Association convened a general meeting of members at the Jiangxi Guild Hall at 4:00 PM yesterday. Over forty people attended, including Huang Baoxiang, Xu Yuangao, Liu Wushu, Xiong Yonglu, Kong Zizhen, Li Jianmin, Rao Junqi, and Liu Changchun. Xiong Yonglu was elected chairman and Kong Zizhen recorder. The meeting proceeded according to established etiquette. The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that since the number of attendees was not large enough for a general election, the meeting would be changed to a discussion session. He hoped that the fellow villagers in attendance would express their opinions on association affairs and the bandit disaster in the province, which would greatly benefit the hometown and association affairs. Rao Junqi then reported on the preparations for the election, stating that the previous election used written notices, which were not easily disseminated to all fellow villagers, so the current election adopted newspaper advertisements. Liu Wushu reported on association affairs: (1) The history of the association, (2) The affairs of previous years, (3) The work of the Bandit Suppression Promotion Association, (4) The financial situation. Afterwards, discussions began. After a long period of discussion and deliberation on the progress of association affairs, it was decided that: (1) All fellow villagers attending today would be investigators, (2) Investigate the addresses of new and old members to prepare for printing a membership directory, (3) The investigation period would be limited to two weeks, (4) The meeting date would be notified using cover notices and newspaper announcements. Finally, Xiong Yonglu gave a supplementary report on the Jiangxi Emergency Relief Fund, stating that disaster relief is like saving oneself and hoping that all fellow villagers would donate generously.

Jintang: Jintang is one of the Zhoushan Islands, about 30 miles from Dinghai County and about 20 miles from Zhenhai. The harbor is winding and the terrain is majestic. The island is densely populated, and many residents come to Shanghai to do business, totaling over 3,000 people. There was no connection between them. Last winter, the Jintang Fellow Association was initiated. After repeated preparatory meetings and the solicitation of members, the inaugural meeting was held the other day at the Ningbo Fellow Association on Xizang Road in this city. Many people attended. Ying Sunling was publicly elected chairman to report on the preparations, and the association's constitution was passed. The meeting also distributed postcards of Jintang scenery, further arousing feelings for the green mountains of the homeland.

Special Documents

Mr. Fei Tang's Second Volume Report (Fifth Continuation)

Summary Translation of Parts Four and Five

Chapter 5: Concerning the Issue of Extraterritoriality Affecting the Public Concession [with remarks, (see Item 2 of the problems mentioned in Chapter 1)]. The chapter mentions a fact: In terms of commercial interests, the main characteristic of the Public Concession's governance system can be summarized as "safety" and nothing more. The issue of safety, the elements upon which it relies, and the extent to which the rule of law within the Public Concession currently depends on the preservation of extraterritoriality, have been discussed in Chapter 9 of Part 2 and Chapters 5 and 6 of Part 3. It is now explained that the specific issue to be addressed is whether maintaining the existing municipal political system established under the Land Regulations depends on the retention of extraterritoriality. This issue has been examined from three aspects: (1) the extraterritorial status of the Municipal Council, (2) the treaty powers as protectors of the Municipal Council's governing authority, and (3) the importance of human rights in local autonomy. The general conclusion reached is as follows: The connection between the municipal system and the extraterritorial system arises from the provisions of the Land Regulations. These provisions are nothing less than a cornerstone, necessary for maintaining the current municipal system of the Public Concession. If this cornerstone is removed, maintaining this municipal system would necessarily rely on the assistance of Chinese courts. However, the current Chinese courts are not yet able to provide this assistance. Moreover, citizens, whether as directors, electors, or civil servants, have been able to utilize this municipal system through their individual activities because of their individual freedom and the security of their lives and property. Both of these are products of extraterritoriality. If the rule of law in China has not yet been established to a degree that ordinary people can exercise their individual rights and fulfill their municipal obligations with full protection, then the abolition of extraterritoriality would inevitably destroy the lifeline of the existing municipal system. If there are no significant elements within society enjoying a freedom of action, such as that currently conferred by extraterritoriality, then the democratic system of local autonomy within the Public Concession will cease to be effective. Foreign police officers within the Public Concession and foreign members of the Volunteer Corps must also have their individual rights protected if they are to continue to perform their duties. The reasons for my conclusion, as stated above, are that the existing municipal system established under the Land Regulations is closely linked to the extraterritorial system, and that, given the current situation in China, the existing municipal system cannot be maintained if extraterritoriality is generally abolished. Therefore, its reliance on extraterritoriality is so profound. However, this view does not mean that the existing system of extraterritoriality must be preserved without modification under an organizational law whose principles are the same as those contained in the Land Regulations in order for the Public Concession's Municipal Council to continue. It is conceivable that the extraterritorial system could undergo a modification, such as applying certain Chinese laws to the extraterritorial courts, as a step towards its eventual abolition, without fundamentally affecting the autonomous system of the Public Concession.

Chapter 6: Under the current circumstances in China, if a genuine system of local autonomy is to be established within the Public Concession, thereby providing a level of safety equivalent to that provided by the Public Concession's existing system, the only appropriate basis is an international agreement. This situation is further discussed below. Therefore, in terms of the situation described herein, the existing basis of the Public Concession's governance system should be maintained. In other words, not accepting a national charter plan (i.e., a charter issued solely on the authority of the National Government, unrelated to any treaty provisions, as a new basis for the Public Concession's governance system) implies adhering to the existing basis of governance. This basis, in fact, is based on an international charter. From what has been stated in the previous parts of this report, it is clear that the Land Regulations of 1869 are far from providing an appropriate organizational law for the Public Concession of today, which has undergone changes with time and circumstances. Therefore, China and the relevant powers should open negotiations to amend the Land Regulations. The Municipal Council, as an organ governing the Public Concession based on its existing organizational law and without any real power over electors and taxpayers, naturally hopes to present a draft plan after consulting with its constituent members, as in the past, indicating the nature of the required changes. It will then submit this plan, through appropriate channels, to the National Government and the powers for consideration. Regarding the description of the Public Concession's existing system of governance as being based on an international charter in fact, and regarding the various levels of adhering to this basis, I do not want outsiders to assume that I am speculating on the final form or method of promulgation of a newly drafted or amended organizational law. Although the final organizational law is promulgated based on international agreement, it may also be issued by the National Government through a granting method. Some may object, arguing that any plan to amend the Land Regulations through international agreement must be adopted only after the relevant countries, including China, are willing to commence such amendment negotiations. However, these countries may not be willing. We must admit that, based on past experience as described in the previous chapter, it is extremely difficult to achieve concerted action among the governments of the relevant countries. Moreover, the National Government's attitude in recent years has shown little support for amending the Land Regulations through international negotiation and agreement. However, if the entire issue can be observed from a different perspective than that traditionally used, the prospects for the future may be completely transformed. I firmly believe that if the facts and considerations described in the previous parts of this report are given due weight, it must be recognized that maintaining the Public Concession's governance system is not only greatly beneficial to various enterprises in Shanghai, such as those involved in shipping, banking, commerce, and industry, as well as the Chinese and foreign residents of the Public Concession who have demonstrated their willingness and ability to cooperate, but also that there is a broad principle of public interest that can align the efforts of China and the representatives of the relevant countries in joint construction. If the position and mission of the Public Concession are properly understood, then the concession is of great significance to China, to the countries that trade with China, and therefore to the world in general. It should not be allowed to endanger its administration by using piecemeal patching methods, or to allow it to drag on as a provocative and pointless topic of international dispute. Furthermore, this suggestion is not a plan that, in the past, was merely viewed as intending to maintain a permanently established foreign administration on Chinese territory. This suggestion is actually a plan to develop a genuine system of international cooperation for the benefit of China and the Public Concession's internal and external interests during the transitional period before recovery, as represented by the countries represented by foreigners inside and outside the Public Concession. If the governments of the relevant countries understand the importance of maintaining a Public Concession's governance system based on international cooperation, then it is not an extravagant hope that each country will cooperate in removing the difficulties and peculiarities that have always hindered the progress of this system and diminished its effectiveness. My undertaking to study the problems requiring reform in the Public Concession's organizational law is based on my firm belief that, in view of the facts stated fairly, there is nothing unreasonable in expecting a necessary method of international cooperation, and I hope that this cooperation can be realized. The issues involved in the changes and reforms currently being discussed cannot be belittled or disregarded because they are merely a preparatory issue for the transitional period before eventual recovery. I have stated my conclusion in a previous chapter that the transitional period is bound to be lengthy, and I have further stated the reasons why the Public Concession's governance system must be continued for many years for the benefit of China itself and the relevant countries. The transitional period not only seems likely to be lengthy, but it is also crucial in determining the nature of future development. The future of Shanghai and its ultimate relationship to China's interests depend particularly on whether the management of the Public Concession's affairs can proceed smoothly during this transitional period. This chapter then discusses Item 3 of the problems mentioned in Chapter 1, namely the organization and tasks of taxpayers, and the organization and election of the Municipal Council's board of directors. The more specific issues arising under this heading are as follows: (1) Should the existing organization of the Taxpayers' Meeting, in which only foreigners have the right to participate, remain unchanged, or should it be changed to achieve one of various objectives, allowing Chinese taxpayers to directly express their views on municipal affairs? (2) Should the tasks of the Taxpayers' Meeting remain unchanged, or should they be restricted to reduce the power retained by taxpayers and increase the power of the Municipal Council? (3) Should the organization of the Municipal Council's board of directors be changed, (A) on the foreign directors' side, (B) on the Chinese directors' side? (4) Should the existing basis of municipal privileges or the existing method of election be changed? Each of these issues is then discussed one by one. Regarding the existing methods for the Chinese and foreign Taxpayers' Meeting, the election of Chinese and foreign directors, the number of directors, the term of office of directors, the time of elections, announcements, and other matters, the various shortcomings have been noted. The report indicates that all arguments noted for evaluation should be discussed jointly with the regulations for Chinese participation in the Taxpayers' Meeting and the various issues of comparing representatives of Chinese and foreign societies. In accordance with the current situation, it is necessary to have separate regulations for Chinese and foreign representatives. This necessity has been acknowledged. The report also indicates that, according to the existing organization of the Municipal Council (five British directors, five Chinese directors, two American directors, two Japanese directors), the number of Chinese representatives is no less than the number of representatives of any other country, and is more than one-third of the total number of directors on the Municipal Council. In addition to the Chinese directors, Chinese society also has the right to elect six Chinese members to serve on various committees within the Municipal Council. In addition to these six committee members, the Education Committee also has three Chinese committee members elected by the original committee members. Therefore, in the three years since the first Chinese directors joined the Municipal Council, there has been definite progress on the issue of Chinese representation. The report then mentions the Chinese society's request for an increase in the number of Chinese directors, so that they would have an absolute majority on the Municipal Council. This request is often based on a debate point, namely that the number of representatives of each society should be proportional to the municipal taxes paid by that society. According to statistics from several years ago, the amount paid by the Chinese accounted for approximately 55% of the total regular municipal tax revenue. Therefore, if there are nine foreign directors, the number of Chinese directors should be eleven. However, it has been indicated that the democratic principle of "no taxation without representation" is very different from the principle that representation should be proportional to taxation. Admitting the former principle does not mean that the latter principle must also be admitted. Allocating the number of representatives of each foreign national society, taking into account the wealth of each society and its contribution to municipal taxes, is certainly reasonable, but this is not the only factor that should be considered. The number of relevant societies, the political experience previously possessed by each society, and the social and educational circumstances of each society that affect its ability to exercise political power are all other factors. Sometimes there is another suggestion, namely that the number of representatives of each society should be proportional to the population, or should be proportional to the number of voters. This suggestion has also been mentioned in the report, and it has been pointed out that if the residents of the Public Concession were all of the same kind, then using the number of votes as the basis for allocating the number of representatives would seem to be a natural plan to adopt. However, such a method would require a public electoral register, without the problem of further distributing the number of representatives due to differences in nationality. The report also mentions the issue of the current voting qualifications, where property interests are a major element of voting rights. In addition, it mentions the prospects for the future, namely that with the passage of time and the widespread of education, the requirements for existing qualifications will be reduced, and if the principle of "one vote, one value" is insisted upon, the need for the element of allocating voting rights by population will increase. However, the report points out that this is only a speculation about the future. As for the current situation, the society of the Public Concession is not of the same kind, but includes people from more than forty countries, representing many vastly different national cultures. Despite recent developments, there are still vast and deep-rooted differences that divide the Chinese society, which makes up the majority of the residents of the Public Concession, from the foreign societies, which make up a small part of the residents. It is impossible to adopt any ideal as the basis for governing representation without regard to the prominent elements of the existing situation. The real question to be considered, hidden behind the various suggestions related to Chinese representation, is whether it is appropriate, in terms of the general interest, to have the Chinese occupy a majority on the board of directors, thereby making them assume a large part of the responsibility for the administration of the Public Concession. Under the organizational law established in accordance with the Land Regulations, allowing the Chinese to occupy a majority on the board of directors would mean transferring the governing power of the Public Concession to the Chinese. When discussing the issue of recovery, it was suggested that there are two fundamental objections to having the Public Concession managed by the Chinese under the current circumstances. The first objection is that under the current system of one-party rule, if the Chinese were to control the Public Concession's political affairs by occupying a majority on the board of directors, the real control would not be in the hands of Chinese people who act freely, as citizens of the Public Concession should, but would actually be in the hands of the National Government or the Kuomintang. This control can be exercised at any time, not only affecting the ordinary administration of the Public Concession, but also fundamentally changing the basis of the current system of governance. In other words, under the current circumstances, allowing the Chinese to occupy a majority on the board of directors may prove to be an indirect but still effective method of recovering the concession. Increasing the number of Chinese directors so that they occupy a majority on the board of directors would place the Chinese directors who make up this majority in a completely false position, because, as far as each individual Chinese director is concerned, they would be assuming an obvious responsibility, and under the current circumstances in China, no individual Chinese citizen, no matter how talented, can shoulder this responsibility. The second objection is that before the Chinese society within the Public Concession can prepare to accept a large part of the responsibility for the administration of the Public Concession, it must go through a period of political education. As stated above, in general, the Chinese society has no experience in using the representative system. Even if individuals have deep attainments in Western learning, it can hardly be said that their leaders have assimilated the principles and ideals contained in the representative system. Practical experience is an essential element of this assimilation. The entire system of public elections, and the entrustment of the management power of public affairs to representatives freely elected by qualified voters, is not something that the Chinese are accustomed to.

Weather Report

According to the Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday, the Yangtze River Basin will be cloudy and hot, with a risk of thunderstorms. There will be fog or drizzle south of Ma'anshan Island. The Shandong coast will be cloudy. There will be temperate cyclones around the East China Sea and the Ryukyu Islands. Elsewhere, the wind will be directionless. There is still no weather report from Taiwan. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the weather in this city was clear, with a maximum temperature of 83.7 degrees and a minimum of 66.9 degrees. On the same day last year, the maximum was 70.5 degrees and the minimum was 67.8 degrees.

Letter

To the Editor: In the Local News section of your esteemed newspaper on the 20th of this month, there was a report about an accident on the 19th involving a British-owned Fourth Road Public Bus in the western suburbs of Shanghai. It stated that the British bus collided with our company's No. 11 bus. This is actually a rumor. Our company's Fourth Road No. 11 bus departed from Xujiahui Station on time according to its regular schedule on that day. When it reached Yangqiang Road, it saw the British bus speeding from behind. Due to the poor road surface and the rain and mud, the British bus driver panicked and swerved and overturned. The location was about ten zhang away from our company's bus, and there was no collision. We respectfully request that your newspaper make a correction to avoid confusion. We would be most grateful. Respectfully yours, to the esteemed editor of the Shen Bao, Shanghai South Public Bus Co., Ltd., June 21.

New Developments at Nanjing Women's Vocational School

Principal Goes to Qingdao to Inspect Vocational Education

Ms. Guo Yangyuan, the principal of Nanjing Women's Vocational School, has spared no effort in promoting vocational education and personally founded the Nanjing Women's Vocational School in the capital. The departments are practical and meet social needs, and the students are also very successful. Recently, she tried to go to Dalian, Jinan, Qingdao and other places to investigate vocational education, in order to learn from it. Recently, she sent a letter to the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute, asking to find a bleaching and dyeing director, with a monthly salary of 200 yuan. If anyone is willing to take this position, please contact the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute, No. 80 Hualong Road.

Development of the Industrial Chemistry Research Institute

The Chinese Industrial Chemistry Research Institute on Rue Pere Robert in this city is sponsored by Mr. Wu Yunchu of the Tianchu MSG Factory. Its nature is the same as the Mellon Institute in the United States and the Institute of Physical and Chemical Research, a public interest incorporated foundation, in Japan. It is established with private donations and serves the public. This type of public academic organization is the first of its kind in the country. Although the institute's location is spacious, due to the increasing development of its business and the recruitment of more researchers, it is feeling inadequate. Furthermore, it is currently leased, which is not a long-term plan. It is heard that the Tianchu MSG Factory is funding the purchase of the Patriotic Girls' School site near Jinan University in Zhenru, approximately thirty acres, and donating it to the institute for the construction of new buildings as a long-term foundation.

Recent News from the Fudan Business School

－Dr. Li Quanshi Devotes Himself to the Development of the School

Dr. Li Quanshi, Dean of the Business School of Fudan University, received an appointment as a full-time professor at Jiaotong University last year and submitted his resignation to the university authorities. After the sincere retention by both the university and the students, he reluctantly agreed to remain as the dean. The development of the school affairs had to wait until he resigned from the full-time professorship at Jiaotong University this year before he could devote himself wholeheartedly. Now a year has passed, and the students requested him based on his previous words. Dean Li, unwilling to disappoint the students' enthusiasm, resigned from his full-time professorship at Jiaotong University to focus on the development of the school's affairs. The students of the school were overjoyed upon hearing the news. Furthermore, the sixth issue of the Business Journal, compiled and printed by the Business Association of the school, has been published. The content is novel and substantial, such as Jin Guobao's "Why and How to Create a Discount Market", Qian Zuling's "The Collection Standards and System of Business Tax", Li Binghuan's "A Review of the Economic Thought of the Austrian School", Zhu Tongjiu's "A Historical Observation of the International Labor Organization", Zou Fang's "New Trends in European Land Equalization", Dai Xinggui's "A Historical Overview of Chinese Economic Thought", Wu Chengxi's "From Foreign Rice Imports to the Production and Marketing of Chinese Wheat and Rice", Liu Jichuan's "The Significance and Characteristics of School Accounting", and Li Jushi's "An Inspection of the International Economic Situation in 1930", etc. All of them, totaling 300,000 words, are the carefully crafted masterpieces of the faculty and students of the school.

The Love-Your-School Campaign of the China Vocational School

The China Vocational School was founded by the China Vocational Education Society and has been established for fourteen years, making it the earliest vocational school in our country. The number of graduates has reached one thousand, all of whom are serving in the industrial and commercial circles in various places and are quite reputable. Recently, with vocational education being valued by society, the number of applicants has increased daily, and the school buildings are insufficient. Therefore, the alumni association and the faculty and staff association have initiated a love-your-school campaign, following the example of fundraising by faculty and students of universities in the East and West, to raise funds by soliciting donations. The opening ceremony was held yesterday morning at 9:00 a.m. In addition to the faculty and students of the whole school, there were also representatives of alumni, and initiators such as former principal Huang Renzhi and Mr. Pan Yangyao, totaling more than one thousand people. The venue was solemn and respectful, and the students were energetic. After performing the etiquette as scheduled, the school song was sung. A kind of enthusiastic and courageous atmosphere permeated the whole venue. It is heard that it is divided into eighteen teams, named after the eighteen provinces, with the goal of 50,000 yuan. It is believed that the school's remarkable achievements will surely be supported by enthusiastic people from the society and graduates from afar, and achieve satisfactory results.

Record of the White Goose Painting Research Banquet

The White Goose Painting Research Institute held its third dinner party at the Deng Tuo Mo Hotel on the evening of the 20th. About 60 people, including the instructors of the institute and the researchers of the sixth term, gathered together, making it a grand occasion. Mr. Hua Lin, a famous literary artist, was specially invited to give a speech. At the beginning of the meeting, Chairman Fang Xuehu reported on the preparation process and the main purpose of the dinner party. Next, Mr. Chen Qiucao, the founder and instructor of the institute, talked about the founding process and the points that the researchers should strive for in the future. The next was Mr. Hua Lin's speech, the general idea of which was to explain the starting point of Western European art and why art is art. At the same time, he also criticized the misunderstanding of general Chinese thought, that art and material desires cannot coexist, and that artists are ill-fated, like peach blossoms, and that all artists should cry in unison, etc., which was passionate and stirring, and moved the listeners. The meal began at 8:00 p.m. During the meal, the researchers' entertainment was added, such as harmonica playing and magic performances, and the atmosphere was very lively. Finally, the Zhaofang Photo Studio came to the venue to take photos. The meeting was adjourned at 10:00 p.m. It is heard that the institute plans to give temporary awards to the researchers with excellent performance in this term, but due to time constraints, it has to be postponed. Jiangsu Holds Public Sports Field

Personnel Summer Training Courses in Various Counties

The Jiangsu Education Department ordered the education bureaus of various counties, stating that the development of mass sports is of great importance to the health of the people and the promotion of the national spirit. At present, it is difficult for public sports fields in various counties to be established in order. It is rare to find those who can truly train the public, make them interested in sports, and obtain good learning results. The department has noticed this and specially organized summer training courses for service personnel of public sports fields in various counties in Jiangsu Province. It will convene all service sports personnel, work hard to train them, so that their academic skills can be improved, so as to improve. In addition to ordering the appointment of Wu Bangwei, director of the Zhenjiang Public Sports Field in Jiangsu Province, and Zhang Zhongfan, director of the Nanjing Public Sports Field in Jiangsu Province, as the directors and deputy directors of the association, and approving the amended regulations proposed by the field, they are to be followed accordingly and submitted to the Ministry of Education and the Jiangsu Provincial Government for record, and notified to the education bureaus of various counties for compliance. A copy of the regulations of the summer training courses is attached, ordering the directors to strictly follow the application procedures and report the names of the recommended personnel for record.

Regulations of the Summer Training Courses for Service

Personnel of Public Sports Fields in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province

Article 1: The purpose of this training course is to improve the knowledge and skills of service personnel of public sports fields in various counties by utilizing the summer vacation, so as to practically improve and develop mass sports. Article 2: This training course is organized by the Zhenjiang Public Sports Field in Jiangsu Province and the Nanjing Public Sports Field in Jiangsu Province, which are commissioned by the Education Department of Jiangsu Province. Article 3: This training course shall have one director and one deputy director, who shall be appointed by the Education Department of Jiangsu Province. Article 4: This training course shall be held in the Zhenjiang Mass Education Museum in Jiangsu Province. Article 5: The training period of this training course shall be four weeks, from July 20th to August 17th, 20th year of the Republic. Article 6: The listeners of this training course shall be limited to those who are over 20 years old, regardless of gender, and have one of the following qualifications, and are recommended by the education bureau of this county: A. Current sports field director or instructor. B. Former sports field director or instructor. C. Current director or instructor of the sports department of the social education organization. Those who have the above-mentioned qualification A in the counties where the sports field has already been established shall not avoid it for any reason. Article 7: The number of listeners in this training course is two per county in this province, but if current primary and secondary school physical education teachers are interested in joining the meeting, they may be recommended by the local county education bureau in addition to the original quota. Article 8: The registration date of this training course is set on July 17th and 18th, from 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and from 1:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m. every day. Article 9: Listeners of this training course shall submit the following documents when registering: 1. Registration form. 2. Recommendation from the county education bureau director. 3. Graduation certificate or service certificate. 4. A recent 4-inch half-length photo (do not glue it on hard paper, write the year, age, origin, and graduated school on the back, and have it signed and stamped by the education bureau director). Only those whose above-mentioned four items are verified to be correct shall be allowed to register. Article 10: The courses of this training course are divided into the following three types: A. Lectures. The lecture subjects are as follows: 1. Academic subjects: Social evolution theory of the Three Principles of the People, introduction to social education, principles of physical education, introduction to social sports, social psychology, sports administration, anthropometry, implementation, construction and equipment of sports fields, theory and practice of track and field, sports referee law, ball training method, first aid, public health. 2. Technical subjects: track and field, football, basketball, tennis, volleyball, national martial arts, apparatus gymnastics, calisthenics, games, dance. 3. Problem discussion: urban social sports problems, rural social sports problems, public sports field organization management problems, industrial and commercial sports class organization problems, distribution and various forms of track and field sports, distribution and scoring problems of ball games, preparation of sports meets, various problems regarding sports refereeing, amateur athlete qualification problems, sports achievement record problems, standard competitions and correspondence competition problems, sports field children's games problems, sports field entertainment equipment problems, popularization of games and sports problems, publicity problems of sports knowledge, connection problems between social sports and school sports. B. Lectures: In addition to the lecturers of this training course, experts and celebrities will be invited to give lectures, and the lecture topics will be announced temporarily. C. Practice: In this training course and nearby sports institutions, practice will be held during extracurricular time. Article 11: Listeners of this training course shall pay seven days of food expenses and three yuan for miscellaneous expenses and lecture notes, which shall be paid by the county education bureau from the social education funds, but the various expenses to be paid by current primary and secondary school teachers shall be paid by the schools concerned. Article 12: The round-trip travel expenses of the listeners of this training course shall be paid by the original schools for the current primary and secondary school teachers, and the county quota shall be paid by the county education bureaus according to the distance of the journey, but shall not exceed the number of expenses to be paid. Article 13: If a lecturer of this training course commits one of the following circumstances, he may be ordered to leave the meeting at any time, and the education bureau shall recover all expenses: 1. Violating the party spirit of the Chinese Kuomintang. 2. Depraved character, not enough to be a model for the people. 3. Poor academic performance, not worth cultivating. 4. Violating the rules of this training course. 5. Repeatedly absent from class without reason. Article 14: Listeners of this training course who pass the performance evaluation after the training period will be issued a completion certificate by the association. Article 15: The expenses of this training course shall be borne by the Zhenjiang Public Sports Field in Jiangsu Province and the Nanjing Public Sports Field in Jiangsu Province. Article 16: These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Education Department of Jiangsu Province, and shall be submitted to the Ministry of Education and the Jiangsu Provincial Government for record.

Open Chinese Doubles Championship Regulations

(1) All amateur players in Shanghai may join the competition. (2) The competition adopts an elimination system and is drawn by the committee. (3) The competition stipulates that Sla Chengjiu balls are the official balls for this competition. If both parties agree, other types of balls may also be used. (4) The competition balls are provided by the association for the finals and the last semi-finals, and the remaining weeks are self-provided. (5) All competitions are held on the grass courts of this association. (6) Each competition is determined by winning three out of five games. (7) Players must hold the competition according to the specified date and shall not postpone it for any reason. In case of rain or accidents, the competition may be postponed, but the secretary of this association must be notified and the competition must be replayed within the nearest period. (8) After each competition, the winner is responsible for notifying the secretary of this association of the results before 6:00 p.m. that evening. (9) The competition dates and results of each week will be published in the newspapers in Shanghai.

Finance

The Standard Gold Price Last Week Started Strong and Then Weakened

Sudden Reaction After the Swap. The standard gold price rose sharply last week, breaking through 800 taels, but the fluctuations were frequent, with ups and downs of about 10 taels per day. After the initial peak, it weakened, and the twists and turns were still not small. It coincided with the swap, and August entered the market. This time, the swap suddenly had a reaction. The shorts initially posted a premium of 1.5 to 2 taels, but later, due to the multiple longs such as Dahut Hengxing, they shorted, and Chengfengyong and others (longs) were unwilling to drop out and planned to show cash, so the shorts were greatly pressured and had to reluctantly post a premium, which was unexpectedly raised to 4 taels. There are about 34,500 unswapped shares, but there are only more than 20,000 shares of spot goods, which cannot offset each other, resulting in the market price being raised. Afterwards, it trended downward. As for July, it only slightly exceeded 810 taels at the beginning of the week. After August entered the market, it turned weak. From the initial opening to the weekend, the total drop in August was 5 taels and 6 coins, and the difference between the high and low prices was 9 taels and 6 coins, but the changes in the overseas silver market were very small, and finally rose slightly. The exchange rate had no honor or disgrace, and the domestic market also had minor increases and decreases. Chinese merchants were mostly long, so short gold was largely in deficit, which was indeed stimulated by the premium posted by the swap longs. The difference between the standard gold price and the exchange rate closing price was still slightly less than 40 to 30 taels, and finally 37 to 38 taels. The number of shares in the exchange was in the range of 50,000 shares. The following is a summary of the situation last week.

Guangbang Swapped More Than 40,000 Shares. Since Monday (June 15th), the large bar was long at 0.0625, the silver price did not change, and the previous order was as before. The domestic market was slightly tight, and the standard gold price in July opened at 798.5 taels. People's hearts were still stable, so it rose by 7 coins, and then returned to 96 taels and 1 coin. Later, because the long sellers released empty air and were unwilling to swap, there was talk of receiving cash, so the shorts were horrified and added to their positions, soaring by more than 7 taels. It reached 803 taels and 9 coins in the afternoon. Swaps had already opened privately in the afternoon, so the price was pushed up to 810 taels and 9 coins. People's hearts were excited. The longs in July turned to August, unpredictable, and the market closed at 808 taels and 1 coin, an increase of 10 taels and 3 coins from last Saturday. Yesterday was Sunday, and all Chinese and foreign foreign banks were not open as usual. All financial and foreign exchange markets had no reports. The Abundance of Settlements and Clearings After the Bank Holiday

The day before yesterday was the summer holiday for the banking industry, so yesterday was a two-day business period, and it was also a day for clearing accounts, so the settlement and clearing situation was particularly vast. It is said that both silver dollar and foreign dollar public slips were very crowded, and small firms also used separate public slips to avoid entanglement and errors. Roughly estimated, the silver public slips totaled about six or seven million, and the foreign public slips were at least around twenty million. Remittances and settlements from various routes also exceeded one million. Banks were closed due to Sunday, so there was no news. In the market, the market price of foreign cents in the morning market was 7 mace, 2 fen, 6 li, 1 hao, 2 hu, 5 si, and in the afternoon market it was 7 mace, 2 fen, 6 li, 3 hao, 7 hu, 5 si for transactions. Morning market remittance drafts amounted to 810,000, and afternoon market amounted to 980,000. Only 10,000 banknotes were transacted in the afternoon market. There was no news of banknotes outside the market. Transactions in small private banks exceeded 400,000. The morning market price of small Jiangnan silver dollars was 6 mace, 4 fen, 6 li and a half, and the afternoon market price was the same, with only 2,500 jiao transacted in the morning market. The morning market price of small Guangdong silver dollars was 6 mace, 4 fen, 3 li, 7 hao and a half, and the afternoon market price was 6 mace, 4 fen, 4 li, 2 hao and a half, with 2,500 jiao transacted in the morning market and 85,000 jiao in the afternoon market. The exchange rate for copper coins was 2,000, resulting in 379,000 copper cash.

Cotton Yarn Market Breaks Free from Deadlock Last Week

Market Prices Trend Higher Daily

Spot Sales are Very Active

The cotton yarn market, which had been brewing for a long time, had the power to rise, but was suppressed by the situation and sellers, so it hovered around the 160 tael mark. Now, spot sales of cotton yarn are developing daily, and the Sichuan and Guangdong cartels are actively purchasing, with huge contract amounts. The Jin-Qing area in the north is also continuing to purchase, mostly domestic yarn. 16s and 20s yarns have been almost completely snapped up, and factories have no spot goods to sell, so they have to switch to purchasing futures for July and August, which shows the enthusiasm of the cartels. At the same time, American cotton, which had been sluggish for a long time, suddenly showed a turnaround, and the sellers appeared uneasy, actively covering their positions. The market prices rose daily, and the prices of yarn in each month were about five or six taels higher than the previous week. The total transaction volume was 236,950 bales. By Friday, the customer cartels had purchased about 17,000 bales of spot yarn, among which the Sichuan, Guangdong, and Tianjin cartels were the most active, with prices rising by three or four taels. There were many transactions among peers, totaling 9,000 bales. It is expected that the yarn market next week will still see an upward trend. Last Week Hankou Standard Cotton Rose by Two Tael

Raw Cotton Arrivals and Sales Both Lacking

The cotton market had been stagnant for a long time, with no vitality. Although the bottom goods were thin, factories had no way to digest them, and foreign cotton was also dull. As a result, the market was in a deadlock. Last week, the yarn market rose sharply, gold prices remained firm, and exchange rates were difficult to rise significantly. At the same time, American cotton suddenly rose, and scattered shorts showed panic, actively covering their positions. The market prices then rose, with each month rising one or two taels compared to the previous week. The total transaction volume for the week was 392,300 dan. Factories did not absorb much spot cotton, and the source was also scarce. American cotton rose by thirty or forty pounds compared to the previous week.

Foreign Cotton Consistently Firm and High

Yesterday, American cotton was strong because of the strength of Wall Street, and short-sellers actively covered their positions, with enthusiastic buying. The market was firm and high, with futures rising by 18 to 21 points and spot prices rising by 20 points. British cotton futures rose by 9 to 10 points, and spot prices rose by 10 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices rose by 15 points. The Indian cotton market was firm. The bulls took some profits, with Pingguo'er rising by 2 rupees, and Aomula and Bailuoxi rising by 3 rupees. Grains and Foods: Rice Market in He Xia Suddenly Sees an Upswing

Xin Zha: Yesterday the weather turned clear, and arrivals from various routes were not many. Sales in this street market were sluggish, but market conditions were rising. Top-grade Changzhou and Wuxi Japonica rice rose by another foot, with limited fluctuations in the middle and secondary grades. The inventory of thin rice was extremely shallow, and buyers were relaxed, so the market was slightly tight at half a Shanghai ounce. Sharp-grain rice sales were brisk, but there was a lack of sharp-grain rice arriving in port. The inventory of customer-grade rice was depleted, so the price uniformly continued to rise by half a jiao. Yesterday, a telegram from Annam reported orders for 250,000 bags of foreign rice. It was said that 50,000 bags could arrive in port within a week. However, although this port has Anhui and Ningbo sharp-grain rice to supply, it has been affected by the gold market recently, and orders have decreased. The retail sales in urban and rural areas mostly focus on Du sharp-grain rice. With fewer ships arriving, Su Kun thick Japonica rice is especially high. Glutinous rice and Yin-hua rice are also tight, and the market price has risen by about one jiao.

Hu Nan: Yesterday, less than ten ships arrived. Sales in this city were more active as the festival had passed. Su Chang thick Japonica rice prices rose by one or two Shanghai ounces. Tongli white Japonica rice and Northern white Japonica rice were slightly in demand due to the relatively low prices. Arrivals were scarce and inventories were thin, and prices rose by nearly one Shanghai ounce. Early and late rice sales in Nan Gang, Qing Jiao, Si Jing, Songjiang, Tinglin, and Zhangyan were sluggish, and arrivals were not many, so the market was firm and stable. Sales of foreign Du sharp-grain rice were even, and prices did not rise or fall. Buyers showed great interest in Yin-hua rice, and the price was tight by one Shanghai ounce. Bai Yuan rice was stable and firm. The amount of rice opened for sale in He Xia was around 2,000 shi.

Silk and Tea: Last Week the Silk Market Remained Difficult to Rise

Overseas Silk Inventory Dwindling... Autumn Sales Gradually Starting

Japanese Silk Sales Remain Strong... Chinese Silk is Severely Affected

Last week in the overseas market, silk mills started weaving autumn silk fabrics, and the consumption of raw silk increased sharply. The inventory of silk was dwindling. The inventory in New York was less than 30,000 bales, and the inventory in Lyon was only over 10,000 bales, which was only enough to meet half a month's demand. Autumn sales of raw silk were gradually starting, and silk prices were trending upward. However, because Japanese merchants actively promoted old silk and sold new silk at low prices, Chinese silk was severely affected. The price of factory silk fluctuated from rising to leveling off, and silk sales were not smooth. The total transaction volume for the week was over 300 bales of various silk products. The export volume of spot silk was only over 400 bales.
