Free Talk

Words of Wisdom

—Qiushui

Lying to cover one's tracks is a necessity for married men, just like the family is for married women.

From what a person eats in the morning, you can tell his character, his profession, his physique, and his nationality, even his family circumstances.

The more a person loves art, the lower his head bows, the messier his hair becomes, and the lower his private morals fall. This is true in eight or nine cases out of ten.

When a man meets a woman he loves, he will never ask how long his love can last, because most men are satisfied with temporary pleasure.

A woman's vanity is born with her heart. If you want to break her vanity, you will break her heart at the same time.

A woman's heart can be as deep and shallow as the ocean and the shoal, but it will never be as clear as the water of a spring lake.

If you want to make modern girls go back and forth in the kitchen, you can only move their kitchen to the car or beauty salon.

Good husbands and perfect lovers are made, not born, and women themselves are the sole manufacturers.

The quality of a person's character is often judged by the number of temptations from the outside world.

The Life of Manchus in the Former Capital

— Cheng Jianhen

The Manchus of Beiping live scattered in the area behind the city. They number in the tens of thousands. During the time of the abdicated Qing Dynasty, they were entitled to imperial stipends and salaries, so they all lived a life of abundance, not engaging in production, but simply eating and sitting idle. After the Qing Dynasty collapsed and the imperial family disintegrated, those who possessed vast wealth could still manage their income and live leisurely lives. However, this was only true for a small portion of them. The rest, who relied solely on imperial stipends, inevitably struggled to make ends meet. They wanted to find employment but lacked any particular skill. Therefore, their lives were extraordinarily difficult. Many of the more astute ones knew that their former nobility was a thing of the past and that clinging to empty titles would only lead to starvation. So, they concealed their Manchu identity and pretended to be Han Chinese. The surnames they used were mostly Zhao, Liu, Guan, Zhang, etc. When asked why they chose these particular surnames, they would stare blankly and be unable to answer. Perhaps they were well-versed in the Romance of the Three Kingdoms? A smile. Since these people pretended to be Han Chinese, they further integrated by marrying Han Chinese. During the time when warlord forces dominated the old capital, most officials who came from the south did not bring their families. Seeking comfort and affection, they often married Manchu women as concubines. This was because Manchu women lived simply and had modest expectations. It was rare for Han Chinese men to marry Manchu women, likely due to class consciousness. After the national capital moved south, the market in Beiping declined sharply. Those who were previously relied upon for food and clothing had become disaster-stricken officials. They could barely take care of themselves, let alone others. As a result, the Manchus' livelihood was pushed to the brink. Out of desperation, many had their daughters pursue the life of a "goddess," meaning prostitution. However, to maintain appearances, they dared not openly solicit customers. Therefore, visitors who wished to experience this kind of pleasure could not easily find their way without the guidance of a "fisherman" (pimp). The above concerns the female side of the story. As for the men, during the days when the Qing Dynasty had not yet fallen, they had nothing to do all day, so they mostly used songs for entertainment. They were quite knowledgeable about theater. They could still handle roles in robes and official hats on stage. Thus, the theater became their only outlet. Among them, some achieved great fame. However, this was limited to those who were proficient in theater studies. Others who engaged in lowly occupations were still numerous. Therefore, the lives of Manchus can be summarized with the two words "tragic" (悲慘). The princes and grandsons of the past had become destitute, which was truly lamentable.

Random Notes on Mongolia and Manchuria

— Liren

Japanese economist Mr. Okura once went to Inner Mongolia to observe the area in person. Recently, he advocated for the construction of large-scale animal husbandry and dairy farms in the area because it is not suitable for cultivation but is very suitable for animal husbandry. If livestock such as sheep, cattle, and horses are raised using scientific methods, and if butter and canned food are made from cow's and sheep's milk and sold to various countries around the world, the profits would be considerable. Recently, Japanese capitalists have felt that this is a profitable venture, and they have each found suitable locations in the area and have begun to build small-scale farms. This type of business has recently attracted the attention of Chinese and Russian parties, and disputes are bound to arise in the future because the industrial movement contains political implications. Recently, a large number of Japanese have moved to various places near the South Manchuria Railway, which has already attracted attention.

Mongolia and Manchuria have always been plagued by bandits, making travel treacherous. Merchants and industrialists are hesitant to move forward. Recently, the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau hired shrewd and capable detectives and trained police dogs in the border area of Harbin to catch thieves, which has been very effective. The dog trainers are experienced Russians. Currently, the most intelligent dog is named "Rex." There is also a dog that is exceptionally brave, able to jump over walls seven feet high and run up and down ordinary wooden ladders with incredible agility. It is said to be a type of British police dog.

Recently, many major banditry cases have been solved and many thieves have been arrested in Mongolia and Manchuria. All of this is due to the work of police dogs. A week ago, someone's sable coat worth five thousand gold coins was stolen. The detective took a police dog to the scene and had it sniff the coat's wrapping. The dog barely touched its nose to it before running to the kitchen and biting the clothing of the cook, who had served the household for five years. He was usually honest and reliable, and no one would have suspected him of being the main person in this theft case. However, after interrogation, he confessed the truth. The pearl was returned to Hepu. Petty thieves will be more cautious from now on. Police dogs are truly a great help to local security. Recently, the police authorities in Harbin, Fengtian, and Jilin have been paying close attention to police dogs.

In recent years, the only storyteller who can rival Li Bokang and stand on equal footing is Su Dao, but the Zhu Lan'an and Zhu Ju'an brothers are a double act. Firstly, the Romance of the Western Chamber that they sing is absolutely unique. Secondly, Lan'an's knowledge and experience far exceed what Bokang can achieve. Thirdly, the Zhu brothers' storytelling skills and their interludes are humorous and witty, improvising based on the scenery. They have inherited the style of Xie Shaoquan, the literary champion. Although their singing voice is not as loud and clear as Li's, their pronunciation is accurate and their rhyme is excellent. Moreover, their audience consists of respectable businesspeople, politicians, and academics. Their appeal is consistently strong and long-lasting, without the problem of fluctuating attendance. Recently, they have been performing The Ingenious Marriage at the Defeyi Restaurant downstairs, and it is also well-organized and logical, similar to The Romance of the Western Chamber. This alone makes them a cut above Bokang.

Zhang Shaochan, Zhao Jiaqiu, Shen Jian'an, and Xue Xiaoqing of the Dongfang Storytelling Theater are two pairs whose artistry is still considerable. However, because they are too familiar with the stories of Shuangzhufeng (Double Pearl Phoenix) and Zhenzhuta (Pearl Pagoda), their appeal cannot be expanded. It is heard that Mr. Chen Xingchun, the manager of the storytelling theater, is determined to revitalize the theater and is working hard to improve it to the best possible state. He will invite Xu Jixiang and Zhu Yaoxiang to join, and transfer Zhang, Zhao, Shen, Xue, and others who are too familiar with the stories. Xu's The Martyrs has been well-known in Shanghai for a long time and has a considerable reputation. Zhu is a disciple of Zhao Xiaoqing and has a reputation for surpassing his teacher. His specialty is the two books Hou Miaojin Feng (After the Gold-painted Phoenix) and Hou Yu Kuilong (After the Jade Kui Dragon), which can be considered the best of their kind. After Zhu Lan'an and Ju'an finish The Romance of the Western Chamber, they will continue with The Ingenious Marriage. It is expected that the Dongfang Storytelling Theater will see a new record.

A Record of the Feast for The Beauty of Yu

— Huan Wu

The Youlian Film Company hosted a banquet at the Xin Xin Restaurant last night to celebrate the successful completion of the sound film The Beauty of Yu, and to bid farewell to engineer Liu Liangchan, who is going to Hong Kong. More than fifty people attended, making it a grand occasion. As the wine flowed, many interesting things happened. Chen Shaomin, known as "The Machine Gun," was the most lively, chattering and joking tirelessly, like a machine gun firing in bursts, truly living up to his name. Xu Qinfang's speech, though brief, was elegant and concise, with a subtle and inexhaustible charm, earning thunderous applause. It was originally planned to have dancing by the male and female employees and actors of Youlian, as well as Jiang Qifeng's ventriloquism, but Jiang suddenly declined due to some reason and did not showcase his skills, which was regrettable. The newcomer female lead, Hu Ping, was graceful and reserved and attracted the most attention. The banquet ended near midnight.

Humorous Divorce Case Judgment

— Jian Fu

I have been addicted to opium for nearly twenty years. I have tried to quit many times, but I have always relapsed, experiencing much bitterness. I have spun a cocoon around myself, and I cannot break free. Recently, with the crackdown on opium becoming increasingly strict, I finally decided to quit. It has been seven months since I last tasted the膏澤 (gooey substance) of opium. The key to relieving boredom is only heavy drinking and deep sleep. So, I have once again formed an inextricable bond with Mr. Du Kang (god of wine). When I wake up with nothing to do, I go with my servant to fish by the stream, washing away my worries. I have a feeling of floating out of the world, and I no longer think about opium. Looking back on the past twenty years of being accompanied by opium, I have always remembered her in my sleep. She is like my dear wife. Now, the divorce case is officially announced. Recalling the past, I am jokingly drafting a humorous divorce case judgment as a form of self-deprecation.

Special Court of the East Asia Democratic Republic, Civil Judgment, Min Zi No. 2709. Plaintiff: Addict, 38 years old, ashen registration, Confucian scholar, lawyer Du Kang selected. Defendant: Opium, 39 years old, black registration, assistant Gao Gen. The above-mentioned plaintiff, Addict, filed a lawsuit against the defendant, Opium, for fraudulent marriage, requesting a divorce. The court has heard the case and judges as follows: (Main Text) The marriage between Addict and Opium is granted a divorce. Other claims are dismissed. (Facts) The plaintiff, Addict, in the third year of the Xuantong reign of the abdicated Qing Dynasty, through matchmakers Heroin and Morphia, engaged a yellow-registered Hibiscus mutabilis as his wife. Before she could marry him, she died. Coincidentally, the daughter of the black-registered Elephant Poppy next door, named Opium, was about the same age. She coveted the plaintiff, Addict's, wealth and constantly sought to meddle. They took the opportunity to lure Heroin and Morphia, and they did not inform the groom's family of Hibiscus mutabilis's death. Instead, they had their daughter, Opium, take her place. They successfully deceived him. Three years later, they chose an auspicious day and consummated the marriage. However, Opium's nature was inherently promiscuous. Addict was young at the time, and his sexual desire was also strong. He was seduced by her and could not practice restraint, eventually becoming emaciated. On March 10th of the twelfth year of the Republic, the couple suddenly turned against each other. Addict sued the defendant, Opium, for promiscuity and childlessness, requesting the annulment of the marriage contract. Opium also counter-sued, claiming that the plaintiff did not know how to restrain his desires and had contracted a chronic illness himself, and she did not want a divorce. The court ordered the lawyers of both parties to mediate and settle the matter. However, on October 20th of the nineteenth year, the original matchmakers, Heroin and Morphia, suddenly told Addict that the defendant, Opium, was actually an imposter. The plaintiff was indignant and filed a lawsuit with the court on the 22nd of the same month, requesting a divorce. (Reasoning) To determine whether the claims made by the plaintiff are true, it is necessary to ascertain whether the testimonies of the original matchmakers, Heroin and Morphia, are accurate. To prove whether the testimonies of Heroin and Morphia are accurate, it is necessary to summon Opium's father, Elephant Poppy, to court for questioning to clarify the truth. According to the court transcript of the 26th of the same month, Elephant Poppy confessed, "I should not have coveted the plaintiff's wealth and had my daughter take her place. In fact, the Hibiscus mutabilis daughter died long ago." Heroin and Morphia testified, "Elephant Poppy promised to give each of us three thousand marks after the matter was completed, but he has not paid us yet." When confronted with this, Elephant Poppy bowed his head and had nothing to say. Therefore, the case of Opium's fraudulent marriage is undoubtedly true. The judgment is as stated in the main text. Prosecutor Xie You of this case performed his duties in court. January 20th of the twentieth year of the Republic. Presiding Judge: Judge Lin Wenzhong. Judge: Shang. Judge: Yong Tao. Court Clerk: Wu Youpei. The right document is certified to be identical to the original.

Rotary Club for Storytelling

Three Eras (13)

— Zhang Henshui

(7) You Are a Good Person

One day, Zhang Xiao San'er was at the East Railway Station seeing off a guest. He saw a crowd gathered on the platform. Pushing his way to the front, he saw two policemen leading a man and a woman away with ropes. He did not recognize the man, but the woman was his own wife, Zhang Er Sao. He could not help but be taken aback. After thinking for a moment, he called his orderly and had him bring one of the policemen over. He asked what the prisoners had done. The policeman said, "This woman is no good. She is the wife of Zhang Xiao San'er, a rickshaw puller. She ran away from her husband and lived with a man surnamed Wang, a clerk, for a few years. Now she has left the man surnamed Wang and run away with a man surnamed Fan. We saw them acting suspiciously at the station and questioned them. This kind of immoral thing, we naturally have to deal with. Commander, do you have any orders?" Zhang Xiao San'er smiled and said, "That's right. I saw you there before. Can't you remember that you used to be a guard at the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce?" The policeman said, "I was a guard." Zhang Xiao San'er smiled and said, "That's all old news. You've been a policeman for quite a few years. Why haven't you been promoted?" The policeman said, "I'm too honest. I don't know how to please my superiors. Commander, maybe you can promote me." Zhang Xiao San'er said, "Okay. I'll promote you. I live on Agricultural and Commerce Street right now. Go find me. Maybe I can think of something for you. You send this pair of bastards to the police department, and then you can come see me." The policeman agreed with a "Yes," saluted, and left. Two hours later, the policeman came to Zhang's mansion to see Commander Zhang. Zhang Xiao San'er's first words were, "Do you recognize me?" The policeman stood at attention and said, "Yes, Commander Zhang." Zhang Xiao smiled and said, "I don't think you recognize me. You beat me up on Agricultural and Commerce Street." The policeman was shocked. Zhang Xiao San'er said, "It's okay. I beat you up too. You caught that man and woman at the station. I thank you for that. Even though you were a little meddlesome, you did a good job meddling." The policeman said, "Commander, policemen don't meddle. This kind of immoral person, it is the responsibility of the police to catch them." Zhang Xiao San'er laughed and said, "Interesting. You haven't forgotten your routine. What good did you get from catching them?" The policeman said, "This is just our responsibility. There's no good in it. Otherwise, what would we be doing with the few dollars of salary we get each month?" Zhang Xiao said, "There's no good in it, so what are you catching them for?" The policeman said, "Commander, this is our responsibility." Zhang Xiao San'er frowned and said, "Don't talk to me about responsibility. I don't understand that. Tell me something that I can understand. What's really going on?" The policeman said, "Yes. We are for society... No. Let me put it this way. This Zhang Er Sao ran away from her husband. We caught her to vent the anger of her husband. Her husband is willing to take her back, and the couple will be reunited..." Zhang Xiao San'er said, "Hmph. Her husband would never be so shameless." The policeman said, "Yes. Her husband won't take her back. If he wants to sue her, the court can punish her. This way, those girls who don't learn good things won't dare to act recklessly. So we took the people's money and still did things for the people." Zhang Xiao San'er said, "That's right. Immoral things must be taken care of. I understand now. You are a good person. I'll talk to your director and make sure you get promoted to sergeant."

Social News

Progress of China's Ivory Carving Industry

Detailed Records from the American Commercial Commissioner. Ivory Guanyin Statues Related to Chinese Culture

Ms. Li Ting, an American, published an article on ivory statistics, describing the development of ivory trade in our country, which is quite interesting. I will copy it as follows:

China is one of the main producing countries of raw materials for ivory art, but there are few records about ivory. It is difficult to obtain accurate figures for the ivory trade. The following records are for ivory shipped from China to the United States. The figures are directly taken from the official survey of the American Commercial Commissioner in China. As for general facts about ivory, there are only two sources that can be relied upon: one is Mrs. Qianbai'er's "Ivory Carving," published by the American Women's Club, and the other is Mr. Laofu's "Ivory in China," published by the Poetry and Art Museum.

The 1929-30 Chinese Yearbook mentions ivory and records the import tariff rate for ivory artifacts, which is said to be 27.5% of its value. It also states that in 1925, 43,670 catties of ivory (from Mongolia or India) were imported into China, with a total value of 177,257 taels of customs silver. Imports increased greatly in 1926, reaching 60,178 catties, with 243,872 taels of customs silver. Imports decreased sharply in 1927, probably due to the internal unrest in China, which reduced the demand for ivory (at least on the part of foreigners). Only 36,973 catties were imported, worth 151,276 taels.

The 1929-30 Chinese Yearbook reveals an interesting fact, namely that in the three years from 1925 to 1927, no ivory was exported from China. This is because already-carved ivory artifacts are not classified as "ivory" but as a common category of "art."

According to the records of the American Commercial Commissioner in China, Guangzhou exported ivory to the United States in 1929 worth US$4,889. The following year, it decreased to US$3,282.

There are 110 shops in Shanghai that make ivory and bone artifacts. Ninety percent of them specialize in ivory artifacts. These American shops and factories are mostly located in the area near the City God Temple. One of them can do 60,000 to 70,000 yuan of business each year. In prosperous years, it can reach 100,000 yuan.

When ivory is imported into Shanghai, each piece is about five to eight feet long. Young elephant tusks are slightly yellow, while old elephant tusks are white and slightly gray. There is also a type of walrus tusk, which is gray and easily distinguished from ivory.

The market price of ivory in Shanghai varies with supply and demand, like other commodities, but averages about 600 to 850 taels per picul. This winter, the price of ivory rose sharply due to the fall in the price of silver. The quantity and value of ivory imported into Shanghai are listed by year as follows:

Quantity (斤) Value (兩)

1924 22,228 97,375

1925 21,959 102,971

1926 33,816 142,275

1927 10,106 41,176

1928 25,858 115,042

After ivory is made into artifacts, its total weight is of course different from when it was imported, because there is a loss of shavings during carving. Approximately nine ounces are lost for every sixteen catties. As for the export of earth ivory, it was 597 catties in 1922, with a total value of US$5,476 (this was not recorded in the recent Chinese Yearbook).

Carving ivory requires skilled techniques, and the wages of Chinese carvers are very low. In Shanghai, ivory chopsticks (plain and uncarved) cost only 3.9 Chinese cents in labor per ten pairs, plain cigarette cases cost only 7 cents per piece, and seals cost 6 cents per piece.

Youth Garden

Staying Up Late

— Zheng Hong

The voices in the dormitory gradually quieted down, and the lights were also turned off. After a long period of silence, a new life began in our room. A group of comrades who were staying up late had roused their spirits and were busy getting active. Two were each reading textbooks in bed by the light of a flashlight. Two others, using a single wax candle, simply sat at the table, copying and reciting, knowing that the dormitory supervisor wouldn't come anyway, so they could do as they pleased.

They were willing to sacrifice a night's sleep because they really had no choice. The upcoming major exam was directly related to whether they would pass or fail. Some subjects usually didn't have exams, but the major exam was unavoidable, and the scores depended entirely on it. So, if they didn't use this one night to prepare for what had been taught over half a year, how could they cope with the exam tomorrow? In reality, if they didn't prepare like this, they could simply turn in a blank paper. If they did prepare, they might get excellent results. Even if they forgot everything they had prepared the day after the exam, as long as they could do well on the exam tomorrow, that was all that mattered. Thinking about the danger of failing and the trouble of retaking the exam next semester, how could they care about losing a night's sleep? Besides, after the exam, they could sleep for several days in a row to make up for it.

The dim candlelight cast eerie shadows in the room. The appearance of the two sitting at the table looked even more haggard and exhausted in this dim light. Their lifeless eyes and barely supported heads, combined with an expression of bitterness, made them look like they were just recovering from a serious illness or about to become seriously ill. It was hard to believe that these two were the lively and cheerful classmates they usually were.

The alarm clock beside one classmate's bed ticked monotonously, and time passed by minute by minute. The two sitting at the table, while preparing, occasionally uttered curses against the school and resentments against the teachers. Anger was building up on their faces, one pale and pitiful, the other flushed and terrifying. One of the classmates preparing in bed had unknowingly fallen asleep. The book fell to the ground. It seemed that when she fell asleep, she had pushed the flashlight, so the flashlight had turned around, and the light was shining directly on her face, revealing a gaping mouth from which came frequent sighing hums. Suddenly, "Oh, I can't stand it anymore..." a startled cry. She suddenly sat up from her sleep, her eyes slowly opening. She looked at the two sitting at the table, picked up the book from the ground, sighed, and lay down again to continue preparing. The two sitting at the table seemed to have heard the not-very-loud cry, but also seemed not to have heard it. They glanced at her. The cry, however, woke up a classmate sleeping in the bed near the door. She had been sleeping soundly and hadn't been staying up late, so she couldn't help but complain, muttering a few words before falling back into a confused sleep. But after that, she couldn't sleep soundly, waking up for no reason from time to time. Finally, with a sigh, she got up, walked back and forth in the room a few times, and then lay down again. The two classmates sitting at the table looked at her with slight surprise. Originally, she was good at sleeping soundly and couldn't be awakened even by loud noises, but tonight she had been awakened by a slight cry and couldn't sleep soundly after waking up. It was probably because her spirits had been weak these past few days, so her nerves had become oversensitive.

The sky outside the window gradually turned white, and the wax candle had burned down a lot. One of the two sitting at the table had fallen asleep on the table. The other one, with red eyes, stared blankly, not knowing what she was looking at, still sitting there in a daze. Suddenly, the one sleeping near the door jumped out of bed, walked to the table, and said, "I suddenly remembered in my dream that I missed two sections during the day and didn't prepare them. Let me do it now. You two are extremely tired, so you should go to sleep for a while. When it's time to get up, I'll come and wake you up." So, she woke up the one who was sleeping, both calling and pushing her, and told her to go to sleep with the other one. Then, in the light of the remaining candle, she sat at the table, opened the book, and gently recited.

An Hour's Lecture

— Cheng

While Ying and I were slowly walking in the corridor, chatting casually, suddenly the director of discipline, Mr. Man, came out of the office and beckoned to us, taking a few steps forward and saying, "You don't have class for the next hour because the drawing teacher, Mr. Shen, is on leave. Now, you two go and tell your whole class not to wander off. I have a few words to talk to you about."

We immediately ran into the classroom as instructed and told everyone what Mr. Man had said. Some of the classmates were overjoyed, while others grumbled, "Who wants to listen to that long-winded Mr. Man? Otherwise, a good hour could have been used to read some novels!" And two of the monitors and two class leaders hurriedly left their seats, abandoning their own work, to sweep the floor, wipe the blackboard, and dust the platform...

As soon as the class bell rang, Mr. Man came in with a smile. The head class leader stood up first, made a gesture to us, and we all understood what he meant, quickly straightened up, and bowed respectfully to Mr. Man. Usually, when other teachers taught, we didn't stand up. Moreover, if we encountered a kind teacher, not only would we not stand up and bow to him, but we would often pretend that we hadn't seen him come in. The most ridiculous thing was that some classmates sometimes didn't even take out the textbooks they were supposed to be using.

"This is a very good opportunity. I have to talk to you for an hour. I've been waiting for several weeks. It's not easy to finally get the chance today," Mr. Man said, standing on one side of the platform, with his hands behind his back, smiling kindly. He was very handsome, not exactly a beauty of the ages, but his elegant conversation and lively, unrestrained, and dignified manner were enough to make us respect and love him.

"What I'm going to talk about now is that there are too many love letters being exchanged among you students. In other stricter schools, not only would love letters be confiscated, but points would also be deducted. Because I couldn't bear to be so stubborn and unreasonable, I have been lenient and, as a rule, returned all the love letters that you young students shouldn't be reading after reviewing them. And I use sincere words to advise you. But you naughty students, seeing that I don't deduct points or scold you much, shamelessly let me advise you once, twice, three times, and you still continue to be unrestrained. I'm now telling you very formally that if I find such a letter next time, I will confiscate it and deduct points. You should know that you are still in the stage of studying. If you don't study diligently and quietly, even if you manage to find a foothold in society in the future, you will definitely feel the lack of various knowledge. If you don't believe me, I'll give you an example. I have a few classmates who almost always looked down on studying when they were in school. They always said, 'In today's society, you have to be good at ingratiating and flattering others to get a good position. Knowledge and experience, no matter how rich or sufficient, are useless.' So they were all very passive and never willing to study for a while. Usually, they were either writing letters or watching movies, entertaining guests, chatting idly, all sorts of idle activities. But now they are barely working in society. And it is at this time that they have learned and regretted their past mistakes. So in their spare time, they are always reading books and studying quietly. Some who are slightly more financially well-off have even hired teachers to make up for what they missed. So if you don't know, that's fine, but if you do know, you should change. In the future, I hope you write less and read less of those worthless love letters, so as not to waste the precious and limited time of your studies. Otherwise, I believe you will definitely regret it when you work in society in the future. You probably all know this saying, 'A youth spent in vain regret in old age,' I sincerely and earnestly pray that this saying doesn't apply to you." He stopped suddenly, his glittering eyes, both stern and kind, shooting at our faces. For a moment, we who had been listening so intently quickly lowered our heads. At that time, I guessed that everyone's hearts had probably rippled a little.

Guidelines for the Youth Corner

(1) The content of the articles should be related to discussions of youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, casual notes, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) Illustrations are limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) We regret that we cannot publish articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese topics.

Marshal Foch's War Diaries from the European Theater

— Translated by Gu Angruo

To inspect the situation in Flanders, I met with General Wilson and Lord Milner in Abbeville. Then, I went to the headquarters of the British Second Army in Brensget. On the evening of the 16th, I met General Buller Me near Kassel, at the place of Kapoor, it was nighttime, all our lights were out, and the sound of artillery fire around us was deafening. The enemy's attack on Flanders was intensifying. I also met General Lopieru, commander of the French Second Cavalry Regiment, and Colonel Ditig, whom I had previously sent to investigate the British troops available for deployment. At ten o'clock, we returned to Buller Me's headquarters in Brensget and called General Weigen, my commander in Shaqes, ordering the 34th Division to drive to Stinwott by car the next day.

On the morning of the 17th, I met with Major General Wilson, the British Chief of Staff. He agreed with the proposals of General Haig and General Buller Me. The British General Staff suggested that the Allied forces in Flanders should successively retreat to the water defenses of Aires-sur-la-Lys, Saint-Omer, and Furnes. I opposed this plan. General Haig had long considered abandoning and even destroying the port of Dunkirk, but I could not share his concerns.

My proposal was to hold our lines firmly for the moment and, when necessary, deploy French reserves and utilize Belgian forces. On the 17th, when I met the King of Belgium and the Chief of Staff of the Belgian Army, I made the same suggestion. Before leaving Brensget and returning to Shaqes, I also instructed General Buller Me on the 18th in accordance with this idea. A few hours later, I wrote to Major General Gilon and General Haig based on this view, as I was very willing to further explain to them the steps the Belgian Army and the British Second Army should take in this situation. Later, I communicated the guidelines for defensive warfare to the Allied forces, also based on this point.

Flanders could no longer afford to cede an inch of ground. Mont Kemmel is only twenty-five miles from Dunkirk. That mountain controls the entire plain leading directly to Dunkirk. If the enemy set up heavy artillery there, he would be able to destroy our resistance and irresistibly approach the port of Dunkirk. In other words, he would be able to reach the Channel coast and endanger our communication with Britain, while also putting the entire Belgian army in a precarious situation.

However, I ultimately failed to prevent the British defensive line in the Ypres Salient from retreating to Dunkirk on April 27, and the Belgian defensive line was also affected and retreated to the Yperlee Canal.

On the afternoon of the 27th, I set off north again. I first went to Brensget to see General Buller Me, then to Ysguebecque to see General Mitry. I told them that the situation was serious and explained to them the fundamental principles of defense required by the current situation. I also solemnly stated that as soon as reinforcements arrived, they must be ordered to enter the front lines to participate in the battle.

From April 17th to 20th, the enemy intensified its attack on the Allied defensive lines south of the Flanders Mountains, suffering a major setback. However, while the Germans suffered heavy losses, the British losses were also considerable. General Haig's letter of April 18th mentioned the extent of the losses. Fortunately, other reserve troops could be deployed to maintain the battle situation. These were the French reserves.

The 34th Division had already set off on April 17th, and the 154th and 39th Divisions were transferred to the front on the 18th. The 27th Division arrived on the 23rd. After these reserve divisions were assembled, they were formed into "the local detachment," commanded by General Mitry. This French force, consisting of five infantry divisions and three cavalry divisions, was deployed from the British defensive line to the north of Ypres. The British Second Army was able to withdraw seven divisions and sixteen brigades from the battle.

However, if the enemy continued to attack relentlessly, we would have to transfer several more French divisions to Flanders. I ordered the Tenth Army to quickly move its vanguard, the 16th Army Corps (31st and 32nd Divisions), forward to the Ouchy-les-Mines line, while continuing to complete its task of assisting the Arras area and preparing to send troops to participate in the battles of Cambrai, Béthune, and Robecq. At the same time, the 46th and 47th Divisions of the Fifth Army subsequently moved to Frevent and Bucquoy.

The French reserves thus underwent a general deployment to the north, motivated by three factors: to assist the British forces in Flanders, to fight alongside the British forces in the Arras area when necessary, and to prepare to participate in the Battle of the Somme.

The dangers on the last two fronts still existed. Conflict could break out again at any time. According to the calculations of the French General Staff, the enemy still had sixty divisions that could try to break the link between the British and French armies. He had not succeeded so far.

South of the Somme River, the fighting on the front lines had been relatively quiet for three weeks, but on April 23rd, a sudden warning arrived. The enemy, with eight divisions, taking advantage of the fog, launched a large-scale attack again. They seized Villers-Bretonneux from the British Fourth Army and Hangard from the French First Army, advancing all the way to the outskirts of Gachy.

The enemy's expansion to Villers-Bretonneux was very unfavorable to our army. The enemy thus gained observation posts and gun positions, from which they could shell our army from a superior position and even occupy Amiens. In other words, the enemy would be able to carry out its plan along the Somme River line, cutting off the Allied communication and even the Allied links.

Villers-Bretonneux was a large area. If the enemy were able to deploy at their leisure, it could become a strategically valuable stronghold. Therefore, at all costs, our army should use all its strength to recapture it immediately.

Therefore, after the warning arrived, I ordered General Rawlinson to prepare to recapture Villers-Bretonneux, as its loss would be a great danger to us, and I agreed with General Digby Jones to launch a counterattack. General Rawlinson was very supportive of this proposal.

On the nights of the 24th and 25th, the Australian troops launched a counterattack, capturing the high ground and villages. The Moroccan Division of the French First Army was on the right flank, retaking the area north of Hangard. General Digby Jones advanced steadily, consolidating the restored positions. At the same time, General Fayolle moved two divisions north in order to participate in the battles between the Somme and the Lys rivers.

The British reserves on the right flank had been fighting near Villers-Bretonneux and suffered heavy losses. General Haig called my attention to this on the evening of the 24th. I gave him a satisfactory reply, saying that the French reserves were ready to assist and that the French First Army had decided to replace General Rawlinson's right flank, the British Third Corps. (To be continued)
